#### SA-4.10 — Use of Approved PIV Products (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that any identity-checking technology the organisation uses to verify staff and contractors is only purchased and installed from an officially approved list. It helps prevent the risk of buying and using untested or unsuitable products that could weaken identity checks, making it easier for unauthorised people to gain access, impersonate employees, or disrupt services.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use a clear purchasing and contracting process that requires products related to personal identity verification (PIV) to be selected only from the approved list. It must include this rule in requests for quotes, purchasing documents, contracts, and service agreements.

Before any product is put into live use, the organisation should confirm that the exact product matches the approved list, keep a record of the evidence, and ensure the system’s security documentation states this rule and clearly assigns responsibility for enforcing it.

##### Approved PIV product gate for procurement and deployment

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the canonical PIV product identifier schema (vendor + exact product name + model + version/firmware), including rules for normalisation, version formatting, and handling of firmware vs software versions | Information Security / IAM Security Owner | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Establish the authoritative approved PIV products list (source-of-truth process, required fields, list version/date, change history, and ownership/approval workflow) | Information Security / IAM Security Owner | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create the pre-deployment procurement/change gate requirements (validation rules, exact-match criteria, exception triggers, and required evidence fields) and document the gate operating procedure | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Update acquisition artefacts and governance documents (security requirements, procurement templates, solicitation language, contract/SLA clauses, and acceptance criteria requiring canonical identifiers) | Procurement / Contracting Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate the gate into existing workflows (requisition intake, change/release approval steps, and enforcement to block ordering/deployment on non-match unless exception is approved) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement audit-ready evidence capture at approval time (record approved-list version, match result, approver identity, linked ticket/reference, and exception justification) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Perform initial reconciliation and drift detection approach (inventory data requirements, reconciliation cadence, reporting format, and remediation process for any detected unapproved items) | IT Asset Management | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Run pilot and operationalise (select representative PIV-related items, test gate end-to-end, refine identifier matching/exception handling, and train stakeholders) | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 176h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set up and manage the official list of Federal Information Processing Standards (FIPS) 201-approved products for all IT components that support Personal Identity Verification (PIV) capability.
- [ ] Define a standard “product identifier” format (supplier name + exact product name + model + version/firmware where relevant) and share it with the procurement and change teams.
- [ ] Add a validation step using an approved list to the procurement and change process, so that requests for PIV products that do not match the approved list cannot move forward.
- [ ] Update the tender documents, purchase paperwork, contracts, and service level agreements (SLAs) so that suppliers must provide only approved-list personal identity verification (PIV) products and the product identifiers for each item, to support acceptance.
- [ ] Set up an exception process for items that are not approved. Each exception must have a named approver and a written reason. Record every exception against the relevant change or procurement ticket.
- [ ] Set up automatic evidence collection for every approval, including the approved list version, the match result, the identity of the approver, and the link to the related ticket.
- [ ] Carry out regular checks to reconcile the deployed personal identity verification (PIV) inventory against the approved list, and fix any differences or record them.


---

#### SA-4.11 — System of Records (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that when the organisation hires an outside supplier to run a system that holds people’s personal records on its behalf, the supplier follows the same legal rules as the organisation for how those records are used, who is allowed to see them, how access is monitored and recorded, and how the records are protected. Without this, personal information could be used for the wrong purposes, seen by the wrong people, not properly tracked, or left insufficiently protected—creating real risks of privacy breaches and loss of trust.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must include these specific Privacy Act requirements in the contract. This includes the required privacy notice, the allowed routine uses, the rules for access and the expectations for recording access, and the safeguarding measures. The organisation must also put in place a clear way to check that the supplier is actually meeting the contract requirements, and require the supplier to provide evidence showing how it has built these requirements into day-to-day operations.

##### Contract clause pack for Privacy Act system-of-records operation

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Draft reusable “Privacy Act system-of-records clause pack” covering (at minimum) system-of-records notice application, permitted routine uses enforcement, access/accounting, and safeguarding requirements | Privacy Officer / Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define measurable contractor obligations and evidence artefacts for each clause pack section (e.g., access logging/retention expectations, audit/report cadence, safeguarding control evidence) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create and publish a requirements traceability matrix template per system of records (mapping clause pack sections to system-of-records notice identifier/version, obligations, and evidence artefacts) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Establish procurement insertion guidance and contract exhibit requirements (mandatory insertion of clause pack, reference to exact system-of-records notice identifier/version, prohibition of vague “as applicable” language) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 10h | — |
| Define contract acceptance criteria and go-live/during-operation evidence checks (including “applied in practice” demonstrations and first operational review cycle requirements) | Contract Manager / Vendor Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 14h | — |
| Implement contract assurance cadence (risk-based quarterly reviews) and evidence review workflow, including sampling approach and escalation triggers for non-compliance | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 18h | — |
| Pilot the clause pack and traceability matrix on one contractor-operated system-of-records contract; capture lessons learned and update pack/exhibits accordingly | Compliance Manager | Business Unit | 20h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 114h |  |
|---|---:|---:|
| Total Estimated Cost | — | £0 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Develop a set of Privacy Act system-of-records clauses covering: how notice is provided, permitted routine uses, how people can access and how records are accounted for, and how information is protected.
- [ ] Create and keep up to date a per-system traceability matrix that links each clause-pack section to the specific system-of-records notice identifier and version, and to the supporting evidence documents.
- [ ] Update procurement templates so that tenders and contracts clearly include the sa-04.11_odp requirements and refer to the traceability matrix as an attachment (exhibit).
- [ ] Define contract acceptance criteria that require go-live and regular proof that the requirements are being followed in everyday operations.
- [ ] Set up a risk-based schedule to review contractor proof of compliance, including samples of access and account records, evidence of safeguarding controls, and evidence that routine-use requirements are being enforced.


---

#### SA-4.12 — Data Ownership (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that when the organisation hires someone else to handle its information, the information remains clearly owned by the organisation and is fully dealt with when the work ends. Without this, a contractor could keep copies of important business records, customer or employee details, or other sensitive information after the contract finishes. That creates legal, financial, and reputational risk if the data is misused or accidentally exposed.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must include clear instructions in every relevant contract about who owns the data and what must happen when the work ends. The contract must state that the contractor must remove all organisation-owned data from its systems and either return it or securely dispose of it exactly as the contract requires.

This must be completed within 30 days of the contract ending, or within 30 days of the organisation deciding the data is no longer needed—whichever comes first. This applies to personal information about identifiable people as well.

The organisation must also check that the contractor provides evidence showing that the data was removed and returned or disposed of on time.

##### Contractual data removal/return within 30 days with evidence

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Draft and approve standard contract schedule “Organisation Data Ownership & Disposition (SA-4(12))”, including dual-trigger (termination or data no longer required, whichever first), 30-day disposition requirement, backup/DR scope, and auditable evidence types | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Review clause language for legal/DP impact (incl. PII/regulated data handling, cross-border considerations, and evidence sufficiency) and produce final approved wording | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Update procurement/contracting templates and workflow gate so contracts cannot be signed without the SA-4(12) schedule attached and evidence fields present/unambiguous | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement operational trigger process for “data no longer required”: define disposition notice format, trigger-date recording, contractor acknowledgement mechanism, and escalation path for non-response | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define contract close-out procedure: evidence request timing within the 30-day window, validation checklist (systems/environments covered, dates, disposition method), and acceptance/recording in contract management repository | Contract Manager / Vendor Manager | Business Unit | 20h | — |
| Run pilot with a small set of active/terminated contractor engagements (including at least one with backups/DR scope) to confirm evidence collection works and disposition deadlines are met; remediate gaps | Compliance Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |
| Produce training and guidance pack for procurement, contract managers, and vendor managers (how to issue disposition notices, what evidence to request, and how to assess completeness) | Operations Lead | Department | 12h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 132h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Draft and get approval for a standard “Organisation Data Ownership & Disposition (SA-4(12))” contract schedule, including the 30-day period that starts when either of the two conditions is met (dual trigger).
- [ ] Update the procurement approval checkpoints so that a contract cannot be signed unless the SA-4(12) schedule is attached and the required evidence is included.
- [ ] Define and publish the organisation’s process for issuing a “data no longer required” notice, including how the start date for the notice is recorded.
- [ ] Train contract managers to issue the final decision notices, track the 30-day deadline, and request supporting evidence from the contractor at the end of the contract.
- [ ] Create an evidence acceptance checklist (return receipt, disposal certificate, and completion statement) and record that the evidence was accepted by the contract deadline.


---

### SA-5 — System Documentation (Control)

This expectation is about making sure there are clear, up-to-date instructions for how a system is set up, run, and used safely. This includes what users and administrators must do, and what they need to watch out for. Without this, people may set up or use the system incorrectly, security and privacy protections may be applied wrongly or not kept up to date, and known weaknesses in powerful administrative functions may be overlooked—leading to avoidable incidents and privacy harm.

The organisation must create or obtain administrator and user documentation for every system, component, and service. This documentation must cover secure configuration, installation, and day-to-day operation (including how to restart safely), how to use and maintain security and privacy features, and the known security weaknesses linked to privileged configuration and use. If the documentation cannot be found, the organisation must record who was contacted, when, and what the outcome was, then recreate the missing material and record the details of the request. Finally, it must share the documentation with the system owner, the system security officer, and system administrators.

##### Maintain complete admin/user system docs with recreate workflow

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define documentation scope model (systems/components/services), required metadata (system identifiers, security category/classification, environments, owners, “last reviewed” field) and distribution rules | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create/approve administrator and user documentation templates with mandatory sections (secure installation, secure configuration, secure operation incl. initial start + secure resume after lapse, security/privacy mechanism use & maintenance, known vulnerabilities/risks tied to privileged/admin configuration/use) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish controlled repository structure and access controls aligned to security classification (including increased protection for vulnerability-relevant documentation) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement documentation completeness checklist and “block publication/release if missing” workflow (required sections non-empty, correct system identifiers, references to security/privacy mechanisms) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Build and run the obtain-or-recreate workflow: log vendor/developer documentation request attempts (dates, contacts, results), create recreation plans, and produce recreated missing content from baselines/runbooks/security advisories | Project Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Execute documentation creation/recreation for all in-scope systems: produce administrator + user docs per system/component/service and ensure operational accuracy (secure start/resume after lapse, admin workflows, runbook alignment) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 80h | — |
| Perform quality and governance review: System Security Officer review of privileged-function vulnerability content; System Owner approval; evidence capture for “last reviewed” and material-change triggers | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

Total Estimated Effort: **236h**  
Total Estimated Cost: **£6,000**

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create templates for administrator and user guides that include the required sections for secure setup, secure installation, and secure day-to-day operation (including how to start again and securely resume after a break in service).
- [ ] For each system, component, or service, assign named roles for: the system owner, the system security officer, and the system administrators, who are responsible for distributing and approving the relevant documentation.
- [ ] Set up an “get it or recreate it” process that records each request attempt, including the date, the contact details used, and the outcome, when the required documentation is missing or does not exist.
- [ ] Recreate any missing documentation using the latest approved configuration standards and the current operational step-by-step guides, and record who recreated it and the date it was completed.
- [ ] Set a regular schedule to review documentation when there are significant security or privacy changes, or changes to privileged functions, and keep records showing the updates were made.
- [ ] Store and share documentation in a controlled repository, using access permissions that match the system’s security level, with extra protection for content that relates to vulnerabilities.


---

### SA-8 — Security and Privacy Engineering Principles (Control)

This requirement is about building and changing systems in a way that protects people’s privacy and reduces the risk of harm. It does this by planning for safety from the start and checking it at every stage. Without this, organisations may accidentally gather more personal information than they need, use it for the wrong purpose, or create weaknesses that attackers could exploit—leading to service disruption, financial loss, or privacy problems for individuals.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set clear security and privacy engineering principles and apply them when specifying, designing, building, deploying, and changing systems, including upgrades where feasible. It must use multiple layers of protection, assess likely threats before building, set clear limits on what the system can and cannot access, use safe default settings, and apply safeguards when buying or changing third-party components.

The organisation must also build privacy into the design by collecting only the minimum data needed, using information only for the stated purpose, providing appropriate consent or notice, carrying out privacy impact assessments, and handling personal data securely. Developers must be trained to follow these principles and apply them to every change, with evidence kept in documented plans, assessments, and design records.

##### SDLC guardrails for security & privacy-by-design artefacts

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Codify security & privacy engineering principles into engineering templates/checklists (layered protections, secure SDLC, boundary delineation, secure-by-default, privacy-by-design, data minimisation/purpose limitation, PIA triggers) | Application Security Engineering Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Define threat modelling gate criteria and artefact schema (use-cases, threat agents, attack patterns, compensating controls) and integrate linkage requirements to design/backlog items | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Define privacy-by-design/PIA gate criteria and evidence schema (triggers for personal data, purpose/retention/access changes; outcomes mapped to design controls) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement CI/CD and change-management workflow enforcement (required artefacts, merge/deploy blocking, risk-accepted exception process with approvals and audit trail) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 72h | £18,000 |
| Create “security & privacy engineering evidence pack” structure and automate evidence capture/versioning in configuration management/release repository (traceability to component version/release) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Establish supply-chain risk controls for third-party/library/container changes (SBOM/provenance capture, dependency risk review workflow, evidence retention) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £12,000 |
| Deliver role-based developer training and record completion evidence referenced by each change package (including gate-specific guidance and examples) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | £9,000 |
| Pilot on representative changes and perform audit-readiness validation (at least one new/changed data flow and one personal-data modification), then tune gates and templates based on findings | Project Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Total Estimated Effort |  |  | **376h** |  |
| Total Estimated Cost |  |  |  | **£45,000** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Turn the organisation’s security and privacy engineering principles into practical engineering templates and checklists, and make sure all change teams use them.
- [ ] Set up software development lifecycle (SDLC) approval checkpoints so that, for any new or changed data flow or security-relevant feature, teams must record and submit a threat model.
- [ ] Set up software development lifecycle (SDLC) approval checkpoints so that privacy impact assessments (PIAs) and privacy risk assessments are required whenever the purpose, data categories, retention period, or access permissions for personal data change.
- [ ] Define and enforce architecture and design rules for clear separation of logical and physical boundaries, and set secure-by-default configuration standards.
- [ ] Include supply-chain risk evidence collection (for example, software bill of materials (SBOM) and provenance, plus a review of dependency risk) in the change request package for updates to third-party components.
- [ ] Record when developers complete security and privacy training, and require that this training completion is referenced in each change’s security and privacy engineering evidence pack.
- [ ] Set up evidence pack retention in configuration management so that all files (artefacts) can be traced back to the specific component versions and releases they came from.
