#### SA-8.18 — Trusted Communications Channels (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that when your systems send **Confidential** or **Secret** (classified) information over network connections, the communication route is truly trustworthy from start to finish. Otherwise, sensitive information could be intercepted, copied, or changed while it is travelling between systems, or the wrong systems could connect and receive information they should not have.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must first identify every system component that sends **Confidential** or **Secret** information over network links. It must then set out the level of protection required for each type of data and for each pair of components that communicate. For every such connection, access must be limited so that only authorised, appropriately trusted endpoints can use it. The information must also be protected while it is in transit, so it cannot be intercepted or altered.

The organisation must document this approach in its procurement and design documents, security planning and architecture, assign clear responsibilities to named roles, and keep records showing that the approach was applied during specification, development, implementation, and any changes.

##### mTLS trusted channels for Confidential/Secret data flows

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Establish trusted-channel scope and authoritative in-scope flow inventory for sa-08.18_odp (source/destination, data classification, dependency level, environment mapping) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define mTLS trusted-channel tiers (Confidential vs Secret) including TLS version/cipher policy, certificate validation rules (SAN/EKU/issuer), revocation checking expectations, and rotation/lifetime targets | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement workload identity and certificate issuance/rotation for service-to-service mTLS (including CA trust model, identity-to-service mapping, and automated renewal) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £18,000 |
| Configure mTLS enforcement for all in-scope service-to-service paths (server/client settings, mutual authentication required, no unauthenticated fallback) across prod/test environments | Platform Engineer | Department | 72h | £6,000 |
| Implement endpoint allow-listing and channel access restrictions (service mesh/ZTNA/network policy rules) mapped to the required tier per flow | Infrastructure Lead | Department | 48h | £4,000 |
| Add CI/CD and deployment-time guardrails (policy-as-code checks to block Confidential/Secret flows without required mTLS tier and allow-list enforcement) | DevOps Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Implement audit evidence collection and operational telemetry (mTLS handshake outcomes, certificate validation results, policy enforcement logs) and integrate with SIEM dashboards | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £10,000 |
| Perform compliance verification and gap remediation for 100% of in-scope flows (test plan, evidence pack, exception handling, re-test) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 384h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £38,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a complete list of every connection between networks where Confidential or Classified (Secret) information is sent, and label each data transfer with its source, destination, and sensitivity level.
- [ ] Define trusted communication tiers (Confidential versus Secret), specifying the required mutual authentication and the required strength of transport security.
- [ ] Provide workload identities and certificates for all in-scope endpoints, and standardise the rules used to check certificate validity.
- [ ] Configure services to use mutual Transport Layer Security (mTLS) (or an equivalent mutual-authenticated connection) and turn off any non-authenticated or weaker fallback connection options.
- [ ] Set up endpoint allow-lists and enforce network and service rules so that only authorised identities can set up each trusted connection.
- [ ] For each in-scope flow, enable and keep audit evidence, including mutual Transport Layer Security (mTLS) connection handshake and telemetry data, the results of certificate checks, and logs showing policy enforcement.
- [ ] Add continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) “policy-as-code” checks to stop deployments that introduce or change Confidential or Secret data flows unless the required trusted-channel tier is in place.


---

#### SA-8.19 — Continuous Protection (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring the part of the system that enforces security rules is always running reliably and is protected, so sensitive information is never left unprotected. Without this, there could be short or hidden periods where unauthorised people gain access, or where the system behaves in an unsafe way during start-up, shutdown, failures, or recovery—including after a successful attack.

The organisation must ensure that every request that could affect security is checked by the enforcement mechanism, that the enforcement mechanism itself cannot be changed by unauthorised people, and that the organisation can prove through analysis and testing that the mechanism is complete and works as intended.

It must also keep the system in a secure condition when errors occur, and recover safely to normal operation, a reduced mode, or an alternative operating mode.

When security settings are changed for different configurations, the organisation must clearly explain why the change is needed for operations, verify that it will not create an insecure state, and show that the change is applied cleanly—without leaving behind conflicting settings from the previous configuration.

##### Always-on reference monitor with fail-closed request gating

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the enforcement boundary and enumerate all security-relevant request paths (web/API/admin, service-to-service, async jobs, message consumers) with a documented “no bypass” routing model | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design fail-closed boot sequencing with readiness barriers (policy-loaded, integrity-verified, dependencies healthy, enforcement active) and specify deny-by-default behaviour when enforcement is unavailable | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 28h | — |
| Implement enforcement mediation in the runtime/request pipeline (e.g., gateway/authorisation layer, service mesh/host enforcement, and any internal client libraries) including explicit bypass prevention and enforcement health checks | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement secure shutdown/restart ordering (stop accepting new requests first, drain/terminate safely, keep enforcement active until request processing ceases) and add runtime guards to prevent “unprotected windows” | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement secure degraded-mode semantics (continue validating requests without relaxing authorisation; define reduced capability rules and safe fallbacks) and add configuration transition controls | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Build audit-ready evidence: automated negative tests for “policy not loaded / enforcement not ready”, induced failure tests (dependency loss, enforcement restart), and request-path completeness verification (including tamper-resistance checks) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Produce operational runbooks and configuration management artefacts (deployment checklist, rollback guidance, monitoring/alerting requirements, change traceability for policy/enforcement updates) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 232h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and record all request paths that could affect security, and confirm they are controlled by the system’s security enforcement components (the reference monitor).
- [ ] Set the system to “fail closed” during startup by keeping listeners and routes disabled until the policy has been loaded and enforcement is confirmed as active.
- [ ] Add integrity checks for the reference monitor and enforcement components, and stop operation (fail closed) if the checks do not pass.
- [ ] Set up an orderly shutdown and restart sequence so the system stops accepting new requests before enforcement is turned off, preventing any time when protection is not active.
- [ ] Define and put in place secure “degraded mode” behaviour that keeps authorisation checks working, without easing or weakening any policy checks.
- [ ] Create and run tests that confirm failures during start-up, restart, and “enforcement unavailable” situations, to prove that unauthorised actions are blocked while the system is transitioning
- [ ] Collect audit-ready proof (timelines, enforcement status reporting, and test results) showing continuous protection across all stages of the system’s lifecycle

#### SA-8.20 — Secure Metadata Management (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the information that describes other information—such as file labels, classifications, and access rules—is treated as important and protected on its own. If these details are not protected, or if they can be changed, people could accidentally or deliberately get around the rules that decide who can see what. This could result in unauthorised disclosure or sensitive information being leaked.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must ensure that the system and all parts that handle this “describing information” correctly connect each label or classification to the right item, apply the organisation’s confidentiality and accuracy requirements to the describing information itself, and check that the describing information is reliable enough to support correct access decisions. This includes protecting describing information even when it is stored separately from the data it refers to, supporting describing information that points to other describing information, and, where the organisation uses multiple sensitivity levels, making sure items that contain describing information are labelled appropriately.

The organisation must define these practices, document them, and assign responsibility for them across the system’s full lifecycle—from planning and design through build, deployment, and change management.

##### Cryptographically protected metadata trust boundary

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the “Metadata Services” trust boundary (logical module) and enforce metadata-only write paths (no direct client writes) including authorised workflows and service identities | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design the metadata integrity envelope: binding fields (resource/object identifier, tenant, environment, version) and cryptographic scheme (signature/MAC), including key/secret management approach and rotation requirements | Security Architect | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement metadata signing/MAC generation in Metadata Services for create/update flows, including versioning, canonicalisation/normalisation rules, and tamper-evident storage of integrity envelopes | Software Lead | Department | 56h | £8,000 |
| Implement fail-closed metadata verification in all enforcement points (authorisation middleware/services), including binding validation, stale-version handling, and auditable security event emission | Security Engineer | Department | 48h | — |
| Implement metadata confidentiality controls: encryption in transit and at rest for metadata APIs and stores; least-privilege access policies for metadata read/write; secure secret handling | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Support self-referential metadata resolution: ensure referenced metadata identifiers are integrity-verified recursively (with cycle detection and bounded resolution) before enforcement | Platform Engineer | Department | 24h | — |
| Add end-to-end tests and evidence: unit/integration tests for tamper scenarios, MLS/label consistency checks (if applicable), and generation of audit-ready logs for integrity failures and metadata update workflows | Quality Assurance Lead | Team | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 264h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £14,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and list all label and classification metadata handlers, and all access-control metadata handlers, and map where the metadata is created, stored, changed, and used.
- [ ] Define a metadata structure that includes fixed (unchangeable) target details, and the metadata values that will be used to enforce the rules.
- [ ] Set up a separate “metadata services” trust boundary that only allows metadata updates through approved workflows and using privileged service identities.
- [ ] Add cryptographic integrity checks (a digital signature or message authentication code (MAC)) to every metadata record, covering both the metadata values and the fields that link the metadata to its intended target.
- [ ] Update all authorisation decision points to check that the metadata has not been altered before using it, and to deny access if the check fails.
- [ ] Require encryption when data is sent and when it is stored for metadata application programming interfaces (APIs) and metadata stores, and apply least-privilege access controls to metadata data.
- [ ] Record and keep audit evidence of any metadata integrity failures and any metadata update events, so they can be used for security monitoring and review.

#### SA-8.21 — Self-analysis (Enhancement)

This requirement is about building in self-checks so the system can check its own condition when it starts and while it is running, and only continue if everything is working as expected. Without these built-in checks, a harmful change, a malfunction, or a temporary fault could go undetected and then spread, causing the hypervisor and critical services to run in an unsafe or incorrect way.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must ensure that the trusted boot firmware, the hypervisor, and the critical service components are designed and built to carry out self-checks at multiple points during operation. They must assess their own internal condition to a limited extent, and verify that the higher-level components they rely on are intact and working correctly, creating a trusted start-up sequence.

The results of these checks must be used to stop or limit the impact of errors so they do not spread, and to confirm that each component’s configuration matches the expected configuration. The organisation must document how this is applied across the full build and change lifecycle, assign named responsibilities, and keep evidence showing it was implemented and verified.

##### Stage-based self-analysis for trusted boot, hypervisor, and services

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define self-analysis scope and stage model (trusted boot firmware, hypervisor, and organisation-defined critical service components) including stage identifiers and fail-closed semantics | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Produce expected configuration baseline: signed/verified firmware & hypervisor image policy, release manifest format (digests/hashes, schema/version, allowed dependency set) and key/certificate trust model | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement root/firmware stage self-test and measurement/attestation recording, including verification of hypervisor via measured/verified boot and generation of auditable evidence | Platform Engineer | Department | 56h | — |
| Implement hypervisor stage pre-start self-analysis: internal sanity checks, hypervisor integrity verification, and verification of each critical service VM/container image + configuration digest against the release manifest | DevOps Lead | Department | 72h | — |
| Implement critical service stage self-analysis: configuration schema/version validation, dependency availability checks, basic functional health checks, and refusal-to-start/accept workload on mismatch | Software Lead | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Enforce fail-closed behaviour and recovery mode runbooks: define safe states (maintenance/recovery/service-offline), implement consistent error reason codes, and update operational procedures for chain-break/config-conflict events | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Integrate stage evidence into central logging/monitoring and alerting (SIEM/observability): pass/fail outcomes, reason codes, timestamps, and chain-break/config-conflict alert rules with test evidence | Security Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Validate end-to-end with test plan and evidence pack: negative tests (tamper/mismatch), configuration conflict scenarios, boot/start refusal verification, and audit-ready documentation mapping to SA-8(21) enhancement | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 352h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] List and document the components involved: trusted boot firmware, the hypervisor, and the critical service components.
- [ ] For each participating component, define and publish the expected configuration baseline, including signed images and the release manifest digest and schema version.
- [ ] Turn on measured and verified boot, and set up the firmware to check the hypervisor and record the device’s proof (attestation) and measurements.
- [ ] Set up a check before the hypervisor starts to confirm that the critical service image and its configuration match the release record (by comparing integrity and configuration digests).
- [ ] In each critical service, run limited self-checks and validate the configuration against the required schema, and record clear pass or fail reasons using specific reason codes.
- [ ] Set the system to “fail closed” so that if one stage fails, the next stage will not start, and a documented safe or recovery mode will be triggered.
- [ ] Add evidence of stage pass/fail results and configuration conflicts to central logging and monitoring, with alerts for broken chains and configuration mismatches.


---

#### SA-8.22 — Accountability and Traceability (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that every important security action can be traced back to the exact person or service that carried it out, and that the records show the correct order of events. Without this, unauthorised activity can be missed, blame can be wrongly assigned, and investigators may not be able to work out what happened after an incident.  

To meet this expectation, your on-premises audit logging and security monitoring setup must record security-relevant actions with clear “who did what for whom” details, link related events across different parts of the system, and keep timestamps consistent so the sequence can be reliably reconstructed. Just as importantly, the audit trail must be protected so only authorised staff can access it, and no one without permission can change, delete, or tamper with the records.

##### Accountability-ready audit events with immutable, ordered storage

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define canonical audit event schema (actor, actor.auth_method, on_behalf_of.target, action/object, correlation_id, event_time/ingest_time) and publish versioned contract + validation rules | Security Architect | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement identity-first enrichment in log collection/audit generation pipeline (authoritative sources for actor and on-behalf-of; delegated/admin actions capture delegator+delegatee; enforce non-empty fields) | SIEM/Logging Engineering Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement end-to-end correlation ID propagation (generation/derivation at workflow start; carry through collectors, SIEM correlation, and audit storage; add schema validation and unit/integration tests) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Configure and validate trustworthy time synchronisation (NTP/PTP configuration, drift thresholds, alerting on anomalies; ensure all components use the same trusted time sources) | Platform/Infrastructure Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement append-only, tamper-evident audit trail storage (immutable write path, RBAC separation, cryptographic signing/chaining per event/batch, integrity verification workflow) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 72h | £18,000 |
| Harden audit trail access paths (separate roles for search/export/admin; enforce strong auth to storage APIs/agents; block modify/delete; ensure unauthorised attempts are denied and logged) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| SOC validation and audit readiness evidence pack (test workflow for ordering via correlation_id; drift alert verification; tamper-evidence verification; produce evidence for SA-8(22) enhancement) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 296h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £18,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define a standard audit event format that includes: the person or system responsible (actor identity), the target acting on behalf of (on-behalf-of target), a reference number to link related events (correlation_id), the time the event happened (event_time), and identifiers for the item and the action taken (object/action identifiers).
- [ ] Set up identity-first enrichment in the on-premises audit logging system to add the “actor” and “on behalf of” details using trusted source systems.
- [ ] Ensure the same correlation identifier is carried through log collection, security information and event management (SIEM) matching, and audit trail storage so that events can be linked end to end.
- [ ] Set up and check that all systems that generate audit records and the security information and event management (SIEM) correlation engine have the correct time, and monitor for time drift with alerts if it occurs.
- [ ] Set up the audit trail storage so records can only be added (append-only) and cannot be altered without detection (for example, using cryptographic signing or linking), and limit administrative access to approved interfaces only.
- [ ] Use least-privilege role-based access control (RBAC) for access to the security information and event management (SIEM) system and audit storage (create separate roles for searching, exporting, and administration), and confirm that unauthorised access is blocked.


---

#### SA-8.23 — Secure Defaults (Enhancement)

This expectation is about ensuring that every system feature that protects people and information starts in a strict, safe configuration. In practice, it should block access by default and only allow actions when there is clear permission. Without this, a system could unintentionally allow access when it is first installed, after updates, or when there are start-up problems—letting unauthorised users enter, carry out privileged actions, or turn off important security logging.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- identify all system components that make access decisions, handle logins, manage permissions, and produce security logs;
- define and document a restrictive default configuration for each component, including what is blocked unless it is explicitly allowed;
- ensure the default “as shipped” settings are controlled and not weakened;
- make sure teams follow the documented procedures throughout the system’s lifecycle; and
- ensure the system either starts securely or refuses security-relevant actions if initial setup fails.

##### Secure-default baselines for authz/authn and security logging

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create in-scope security-function component map (authn/authz/logging + integration points + degraded/fallback modes) and obtain sign-off | Security Architect | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define secure-default rules per component (deny-by-default access model, explicit RBAC/ABAC, no permissive fallbacks, well-formed/policy-consistent request requirements) and document as auditable baseline | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement fail-closed initialisation behaviour for security dependencies (token validation, policy/keys/metadata fetch, authorisation dependency, logging dependency) including configuration switches and safe refusal/deny logic | Software Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Codify secure-default baselines as configuration-as-code (IaC/templates) for authn/authz and security logging across environments, including enforcement to prevent unauthorised weakening | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement/adjust authorisation enforcement to remove implicit admin roles and ensure explicit privilege checks for privileged actions (including service-to-service auth) | Security Engineer | Department | 40h | — |
| Implement/standardise security logging defaults for authentication/authorisation outcomes (allow/deny, privilege-relevant actions), including correlation IDs and structured event schema | DevOps Lead | Department | 32h | — |
| Build automated verification suite (config checks + integration tests for deny-by-default and fail-closed scenarios; evidence outputs for CI/CD) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 224h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] List all in-scope security features for the application, including how they connect to authentication (authn), authorisation (authz), and logging.
- [ ] Set “deny by default” secure default rules for every component, including privileged actions, with clear allow conditions that follow the agreed policy.
- [ ] Set the system to fail closed during start-up if security services (token validation, policy checks, and logging) are not available.
- [ ] Create a “secure by default” baseline configuration for authentication (authn), authorisation (authz), and security logging, and enforce it by using continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) checks.
- [ ] Turn on audit logging for authentication and authorisation by default, and send it to the security information and event management (SIEM) logging pipeline using verified default settings.
- [ ] Create and run automated tests to prove that unauthorised requests are blocked by default, and that scenarios where initial setup fails remain secure.


---

#### SA-8.24 — Secure Failure and Recovery (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure that when a security protection fails, the system does not accidentally allow unauthorised access, and that when it recovers, it returns to a safe operating state. Without this, a failure could leave services partly working in a way that allows unauthorised people to gain access, or it could cause recovery actions to undo protections and create new security weaknesses.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must design, document, and put in place how its information system and its security failure-handling and recovery processes behave at every stage of use, including start-up, normal operation, shutdown, and maintenance. The system must detect security-related failures within its defined limits and, by default, move into a safe “block access” state. It must also handle interruptions without leaving permissions or data in an unsafe combination, and it must keep security protections in place even during any reconfiguration.

If recovery is needed, the system must restore service in a normal, reduced, or alternative secure mode without breaking its security rules. This should be done using safe switching, returning to a secure previous state, or shutting down securely when recovery is not possible. The organisation must keep clear records and have contingency procedures that are tested.

##### Fail-closed security enforcement with secure recovery cutover

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Component secure failure/recovery behaviour mapping for sa-8.24_prm_1 (initialisation, normal operation, shutdown, maintenance) including deny-by-default and recovery options | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define and approve “secure failure” and “secure recovery” decision logic (degraded secure mode vs secure shutdown/rollback) with operational limits and triggers | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement deny-by-default enforcement boundary (e.g., API gateway/reverse proxy/service mesh policy point) with safe failure outcomes and dependency health gating | Platform Engineer | Department | 56h | £18,000 |
| Implement continuous enforcement during reconfiguration (failover/cutover/rollback) with staged cutover orchestration and zero-bypass guarantees | DevOps Lead | Department | 48h | £6,000 |
| Implement secure recovery mechanisms: degraded/alternative secure mode runbooks and automated rollback to known-good configuration/release | Operations Lead | Department | 40h | £4,000 |
| Implement failure detection and auditable evidence: health checks, failure condition taxonomy, and security event logging to SIEM (timestamps, component identifiers, action taken) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £3,500 |
| Validation and assurance: tabletop + automated integration tests for failure/recovery scenarios; evidence pack for SA-8(24) audit readiness | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Production readiness: update runbooks, change management artefacts, monitoring dashboards/alerts, and perform controlled deployment with rollback plan | Service Delivery Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |

Total Estimated Effort: **272h**  
Total Estimated Cost: **£31,500**

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and document the specific security failure response and recovery methods in **sa-8.24_prm_1** during start-up, normal operation, shutdown, and maintenance.
- [ ] Set the security enforcement boundary to “deny by default” if security-critical dependencies—identity, policy, or key material—are unhealthy or cannot be reached.
- [ ] Set up health checks and failure alerts for security-critical functions, within the agreed operating limits.
- [ ] Treat failover, cutover, and rollback as security-critical processes, with a staged cutover, to prevent any time when security rules could be bypassed.
- [ ] Set up recovery options so that, after a failure, the system either continues running in a reduced but secure mode or safely shuts down and rolls back to a previously verified secure state.
- [ ] Create and keep audit and log records showing the detected failures and the secure failure and recovery action that was chosen, including the date and time and the identifiers for the affected components.


---

#### SA-8.25 — Economic Security (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure your security decisions for systems that handle Confidential and Secret information are sensible and good value, not too much and not too little. If you do not take this approach, you could end up paying for protection that is stronger than needed, or you could spend too little on protection that would have helped prevent serious harm from a breach. You may also fail to collect enough credible evidence that your safeguards actually work.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use a documented cost–benefit approach when specifying, designing, building, implementing, and changing the in-scope systems and components. Security measures must be selected so that their cost is no more than the potential harm they help prevent. The organisation must also balance the expected value of assurance activities (the confidence gained from credible evidence) against the effort and cost of obtaining that evidence.

The organisation must record the results and carry them forward into acquisition policies, design documents, security and privacy requirements, the overall security design, and the system security plan. Named individuals must be responsible for producing, applying, and reviewing the justification.

##### Economic security cost–benefit gates for Confidential/Secret components

- Category: Software
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define “economic security scope” tagging approach and update CMDB/architecture schema for Confidential/Secret components (including data classification mapping rules) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create standard economic security artefact templates (harm/damage model, control mechanism cost model, mechanism selection rationale, assurance/evidence plan, assurance cost/effort estimate, traceability matrix) and publish guidance for completion | Security Architect | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code gates in the design/change approval workflow (required fields, traceability completeness, and system security plan reference checks) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 56h | £12,000 |
| Integrate policy-as-code checks with existing tooling (e.g., ticketing/workflow, architecture repository, and evidence/traceability sources) and produce automated validation reports for audit | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £8,000 |
| Build a lightweight economic security decision record generator/workflow form (including “delta economic security” update mode) and ensure it is mandatory for in-scope changes | Software Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Pilot the gated process on 2–3 representative Confidential/Secret components and refine thresholds/wording for harm, cost, and assurance credibility to reduce rework | Project Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |
| Establish operational cadence: annual revalidation process and material-change triggers; define ownership, review SLAs, and evidence retention expectations | Governance/Compliance Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Deliver training and adoption support (workshops + job aids) for Application/Product Owners and Change/Release Managers; confirm readiness via sign-off checklist | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | £2,500 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 280h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £28,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an in-scope tagging rule for systems and components that handle Confidential and Secret data, in the architecture repository and configuration management database (CMDB).
- [ ] Define standard templates for economic security evidence and analysis, including: a harm model, a mechanism cost model, an assurance and evidence plan, and a traceability matrix.
- [ ] Set up “policy-as-code” workflow checkpoints that only allow design or change approval after the required economic security documents are provided and the actions can be traced back to who did what and when.
- [ ] Include references to economic security decision records in updates to the system security plan for all in-scope changes.
- [ ] Set a review schedule (at least once a year, plus when there are significant changes) and require updated information on economic security whenever those changes occur.
- [ ] Train application and security architects on how to produce clear, auditable cost–benefit justifications and realistic evidence plans

#### SA-8.26 — Performance Security (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure security protections are built in a way that does not unnecessarily slow the organisation’s systems down. Without this, stronger protections—such as secure access checks, protecting sensitive data, and keeping detailed records of activity—could make services slow or unreliable. That can cause delays, workarounds, or even failures during busy periods.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must design, build, and maintain the system and the parts that affect security so that performance and security needs are clearly defined, prioritised, and balanced from the start. It must assess how much each security feature affects performance, especially the more demanding ones, and record why any compromise is acceptable.

Where possible, it should use the most efficient security measures available, including simpler components that add less overhead. The organisation must apply and document this “performance versus security” approach throughout specification, design, development, implementation, and changes, and keep the relevant approved documents and trade-off analysis up to date.

##### Performance-security design gate with measured trade-off evidence

- Category: Software
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create performance-security design gate template (requirements, performance budgets, prioritisation rules, acceptance thresholds, evidence checklist) | Security Engineering Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define trade-off analysis methodology and evidence standards (measured vs validated estimate, assumptions, monitoring plan, approval criteria) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code gate in CI/CD and IaC workflows (required artefacts, completeness checks, and blocking rules for security-relevant design changes) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Build integration for automated evidence capture (link gate artefacts to change tickets/releases; generate audit-ready records and versioning) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | £3,000 |
| Establish performance baseline and regression test approach for security overhead (KPI selection, staging/load test plan, peak/normal scenarios, correlation to security events) | Performance Engineering / SRE Lead | Department | 32h | £8,000 |
| Develop and run initial end-to-end pilot for representative security changes (e.g., auth hardening, crypto/cipher changes, logging/telemetry adjustments) with documented trade-off records | Application Security Architect | Business Unit | 24h | £2,500 |
| Operationalise governance: approvals, training, and audit readiness (runbooks, RACI, developer guidance, quarterly review cadence, audit sampling support) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

Total Estimated Effort: **176h**  
Total Estimated Cost: **£19,500**

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a template for performance and security requirements that covers security-relevant parts, performance limits (budgets), how priorities are decided, and the criteria for accepting results (acceptance thresholds).
- [ ] Define a trade-off analysis standard for security overhead, including the types of evidence to use, the assumptions to make, and the monitoring and verification plan, covering cryptography.
- [ ] Add automated “policy-as-code” checks to the continuous integration/continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipeline so that security-relevant deployments are blocked unless the deployment template and the documented trade-off evidence have been approved and linked to the change ticket.
- [ ] Run the most resource-intensive security services (for example, authentication, encryption, and key management) in the staging environment under conditions that match the expected peak load, to establish baseline performance and operating profile.
- [ ] Require teams to explicitly choose and justify the minimum-overhead security measures they will use, including considering less computationally intensive alternatives where they are sufficient.
- [ ] Set up automated checks to detect regressions in telemetry results when security settings are changed, and confirm that any extra workload after deployment stays within the agreed limits.
- [ ] Update and version the system security plan and architecture, and keep audit-ready records of the agreed trade-offs for every approved change.

#### SA-8.27 — Human Factored Security (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making the tools used by system administrators and operators to set up and manage security clear, sensible, and safe to use. If these screens and tools are confusing, slow, or unhelpful, people may make mistakes, misunderstand what a change will do, or become frustrated and turn off protections. That can leave systems more exposed than intended.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must define and document how “human-friendly” design will be applied to privileged access and security configuration screens and tools. It must also include plain usability expectations in the system’s security requirements. The organisation must carry out usability analysis, record the plan and responsibilities, and involve the right teams so that information security reviews and approves the approach.

The organisation must ensure the interfaces provide meaningful feedback and clear warnings when changes affect security. They must enforce protections without being intrusive, help administrators understand the impact of their choices, and ensure that what users intend is what the system actually enforces—both before start-up and during day-to-day operation. The organisation must also keep evidence showing these practices were considered and improved during design and change work.

##### Human-factored UX for PAM and security configuration consoles

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Create Human-Factored Security UX Standard for PAM/security configuration consoles (patterns, terminology, warning taxonomy, measurable usability/safety requirements, evidence requirements) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Define “intent-to-enforcement” mapping requirements for all security-policy-changing actions (security-impact summary fields, before/after diff rules, effective-state display, step-up authentication triggers, follow-up/restart messaging) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement UI guardrails in the PAM/configuration console (security-impact summary, contextual warnings, progressive disclosure, diff/preview components, non-intrusive enforcement patterns) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 120h | — |
| Implement effective-state confirmation and post-action feedback (exact setting changed, enforced policy state, required follow-up steps, audit-friendly messaging hooks) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 72h | — |
| Add usability analysis and iteration cycle with representative admin/operator users (test plan, moderated sessions, task/error metrics, remediation backlog, UX standard updates) | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 56h | £8,000 |
| Establish governance workflow and audit-ready evidence pack (UX change approval process, design rationale, traceability from UI behaviour to enforcement outcomes, release/change record templates) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Instrumentation and validation for intent-to-enforcement correctness (logging/telemetry for UI warnings shown vs enforcement outcomes, dashboards for error rates, regression test cases) | Security Engineer | Department | 64h | £6,000 |
| Total Estimated Effort |  |  | **424h** |  |
| Total Estimated Cost |  |  |  | **£14,000** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a human-focused security user experience (UX) standard for privileged access management (PAM) and security configuration screens. This standard should cover warnings, confirmation prompts, and feedback that clearly shows the current effective setting.
- [ ] For every workflow in the PAM (privileged access management) and configuration user interface that changes a security policy, provide a plain-language summary of the security impact and show what will change before and after the update.
- [ ] Add clear, specific warnings when choices are insecure or high risk, and require step-up authentication only when the risk meaningfully increases.
- [ ] After enforcement, confirm that the change has taken effect, and complete any required follow-up actions (approval still needed, re-authentication, or restart/service impact).
- [ ] Run usability testing sessions with representative administrators and operators, record the results, agreed fixes, and the approval (sign-off) evidence.
- [ ] Set up an approval process for user experience (UX) changes that affect security controls, including review by Security Engineering and Information Security and keeping complete, audit-ready records of each change.

#### SA-8.28 — Acceptable Security (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure your customer-facing website and mobile apps protect people’s privacy in a way that feels right to users and works smoothly, not confusingly. If privacy protections are unclear, too slow, or difficult to control, users may stop using the service, use it in unintended ways, or take risky workarounds. This can result in personal information being shared or handled incorrectly.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly set out what users should reasonably expect for both privacy and performance, based on its privacy policy and the app’s intended design. It must then build those expectations into the app’s requirements, design, overall system planning, day-to-day development, and any changes.  

Users must be able to easily limit privacy-related actions, and privacy messages must be clear and match what the system actually does. The organisation must document how it will achieve this, assess privacy impacts and privacy risks, keep the records, and ensure the same user experience works properly on both the website and mobile apps.

- Priority: Critical

- [ ] Set clear, measurable expectations for privacy controls and performance for the main user journeys, and document the platform-specific requirements for both web and mobile.
- [ ] Put privacy restrictions into the backend so they truly block processing (not just what users see on the screen), and make sure the control behaviour is consistent across all platforms.
- [ ] Add automated tests in the continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipeline to check that privacy notices and controls are present, correct, and remain in place. Include negative tests to confirm that restricted actions are blocked.
- [ ] Set performance limits for the defined customer journeys (for example, maximum acceptable delays, error rates, and timeouts). Only allow a release if these limits are met; otherwise, stop the build from completing.
- [ ] Carry out usability and privacy understanding testing to confirm that users can clearly understand and correctly use the privacy controls to protect their privacy, without needing unsafe workarounds.
- [ ] Create a clear audit trail showing how each contract requirement links to the relevant privacy policy sections, the design documents, and the records of any changes made.

#### SA-8.29 — Repeatable and Documented Procedures (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure your on-premises systems are built, configured, and changed in a way that can be repeated and is fully documented. That way, the same system can be recreated correctly later. Without this, you risk making changes that are inconsistent or incomplete, having unclear security settings, and being unable to clearly show what was done and why—particularly when staff leave, systems are rebuilt, or you need to investigate an issue.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must:
- identify which on-premises components are in scope, and which security-relevant configuration items are covered; and
- create clear, step-by-step procedures for producing security requirements, designing, developing, implementing, and modifying those items across the entire lifecycle.

These procedures must be detailed enough for someone else to rebuild the component, and the outcomes must match the records you keep.

You must also keep relevant documentation up to date and consistent, such as:
- system design
- security and privacy requirements
- security architecture
- the system security plan
- other relevant records

Finally, you must ensure your acquisition (procurement) policy includes these procedures, with named roles responsible for setting requirements, carrying out lifecycle activities, and providing security oversight.

- [ ] Maintain author-controlled, version-managed procedure packs covering requirements, design, secure development, secure implementation, and secure changes (modifications)
- [ ] Create repeatable, rule-based build and deployment files for each in-scope component, and store them in a controlled repository.
- [ ] Automate the creation and storage of configuration snapshots and exports, test results, and drift and compliance reports for each build or rebuild.
- [ ] For each release or rebuild record, link it to the exact procedure pack version and build artefact version in your release evidence store.
- [ ] Update the system design and security plan documents to reference the procedure pack versions used for the current component state.

#### SA-8.30 — Procedural Rigor (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure your systems are designed and changed in a controlled, well-documented way, so the final result is correct and matches the plan. Without this, teams could accidentally add features that were never intended, use outdated or misleading design information, or make changes based on assumptions about how something works. This can create weaknesses that are difficult to spot and fix later.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set out clear, documented procedures covering the full process—from planning and design, through building and putting the system into service, to later updates—for the most important parts, such as sign-in, who can access what, protection of data, recording key events, and network protections. These procedures must include checks and approvals, require design documents to be produced and kept accurate so they match what is actually built, and ensure changes are made using the latest design information rather than guessing or working backwards.

The required level of detail must match how much the system needs to be trusted: higher trust requires more rigorous work and stronger evidence.

##### Procedural-rigor SDLC gates with authoritative design as source of truth

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Produce lifecycle procedure templates for security-relevant components (design/spec, build/config, deploy/implementation, modification) with defined inputs/outputs, evidence requirements, and “as-built” capture expectations | Security Engineering Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Define authoritative design record structure and governance (design artefact taxonomy, versioning rules, interface/security behaviour documentation standards, exception workflow and time-bounding) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 48h | — |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep an up-to-date list of the security-relevant components that are in scope for SA-08.30_odp, including authentication, access control, encryption, logging, and network security.
- [ ] Define levels of procedural strictness linked to trustworthiness levels, including the required reviews, the types of evidence to provide, and the roles authorised to approve.
- [ ] Publish lifecycle procedure templates that set out the required security design deliverables and the proof needed to verify them for design, building/configuration, deployment, and changes (modifications).
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipelines, or release gates, that stop security-relevant deployments unless all of the following are in place: complete documentation, clear traceability, approvals from separate roles, and proof that required checks have been completed.
- [ ] Require every security-relevant change to update the official design records and to include the “as-built” configuration and security baseline evidence in the same change package (or record an approved exception).
- [ ] Automate checks that compare the current “as built” configuration against the approved design (for example, by exporting configuration data and running compliance scans against the required policies and configurations), and save the results for audit purposes.


---

#### SA-8.31 — Secure System Modification (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that when your organisation changes or upgrades any systems that are important for security, the change does not quietly weaken protection. Without this, a routine update, software patch, or settings change could unintentionally break safeguards, increase the risk of unauthorised access, or stop key protections from working as intended—leaving the organisation exposed in ways that are difficult to spot until it is too late.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must apply the same careful, disciplined approach used when the system was first designed and built to every later change to all parts that affect security. Before any change is put into live use, it must be assessed for its security impact and checked against the organisation’s agreed level of acceptable risk, with the results recorded. Changes must be managed through formal change records and configuration tracking, with clear approvals and supporting documentation, and the system’s configuration records must be updated to match what was actually deployed.

##### Secure change gate with pre-deployment security analysis evidence

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define and document the scope of “security-relevant” changes for the application’s multi-tier architecture (including IT and OT-adjacent where applicable), with clear inclusion/exclusion criteria and examples | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create the Secure Modification Procedure and Security Impact Assessment (SIA) template, including required SIA sections (affected security requirements, impacts, risk outcome, explicit rollback/contingency plan) and evidence requirements | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Configure the ITSM/release workflow gate to block deployment/operational use unless the change record contains: completed SIA reference, required approvals (security + system/application owner), and pre-deployment evidence timestamp | Project Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement change record-to-configuration binding: enforce mandatory links from change records to relevant configuration items (IaC modules, build artefacts, container images, DB migration scripts, network/security policy objects) and define the “as-built” evidence expectations | Configuration Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Update configuration management/CMDB processes to ensure approved changes result in baseline updates that match deployed “as-built” state (including ownership for verification and sign-off) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish audit-ready evidence handling: define retention, naming conventions, and audit trail requirements for SIA outputs, approvals, and rollback plans; align with existing governance and audit processes | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| (Where feasible) Add automated validation hooks and record results back to the change record (e.g., config drift checks, logging/telemetry endpoint verification, encryption setting verification, authorisation policy/role verification) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Pilot the secure change gate on a representative set of security-relevant change types, refine the procedure/workflow based on findings, and roll out training to change authors and approvers | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 256h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document which systems and components, and which types of changes, are considered security-relevant for this application.
- [ ] Create a secure change process that requires, before deployment, a Security Impact Assessment mapped to the security requirements and each stakeholder’s acceptable level of risk.
- [ ] Set up the IT service management (ITSM) and release process so that deployments are blocked unless the change record includes completed security information and assurance (SIA) evidence and the required security and system approvals.
- [ ] Update the configuration management requirements so that every approved change updates the configuration management database (CMDB) and the approved configuration baselines to match the actual “as-built” system that has been deployed.
- [ ] After deployment, automatically run security checks (for example, confirm the system has not drifted from its secure baseline, confirm logging and monitoring are enabled, and confirm encryption and access rules are in place) and record the results in the change record.
- [ ] Train application, platform, and security reviewers on the secure change procedure and what evidence and approvals are expected


---

#### SA-8.32 — Sufficient Documentation (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the people who build, run, and change your on-premises systems have clear, up-to-date instructions for the security measures that protect access, record activity, and safeguard sensitive data. Without this, staff may set security controls incorrectly or misunderstand how they are meant to work. This can lead to unauthorised access, important events not being recorded, or sensitive data being left unprotected.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must provide and keep a well-organised set of security documents and role-based training. This should cover:
- **Identity** (who can access)
- **Logging** (what activity is recorded)
- **Access control** (who can do what)
- **Encryption services** (how data is protected)

The training and documents must also include plain-language explanations of what can go wrong if settings are used incorrectly or are set up wrongly.

These documents and training must be kept current as the system is specified, designed, developed, implemented, and changed. There must be clear responsibility for updating them, version-controlled records, and evidence that the relevant roles can find the latest guidance and explain the risks correctly.

##### Role-based security docs and training for identity, logging, access, encryption

- Category: Manual
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define the “Security Sufficient Documentation” standard (scope, templates, naming/versioning, approval workflow, evidence requirements) aligned to NIST SP 800-53 SA-8(32) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create the version-controlled documentation repository structure and templates for: Identity services, Logging/monitoring, Access control, Encryption services (including sections for purpose, usage, verification, misuse/misconfiguration risks, ownership/last reviewed) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | £3,000 |
| Produce component documentation content for the on-prem system: Identity services (MFA, service accounts, lifecycle, privileged access), Logging/monitoring (events, routing to SIEM, retention/integrity expectations, alerting hooks) | Security Engineer | Department | 32h | — |
| Produce component documentation content for the on-prem system: Access control (role model, least privilege, authorisation decision points, segregation of duties, privileged workflows) and Encryption services (what’s encrypted, key/cert responsibilities, rotation expectations, failure modes) | Security Engineer | Department | 32h | — |
| Link each documentation section to the system configuration source of truth (IdP/IAM objects, SIEM/agent policies, authorisation policy definitions, KMS/certificate records) with environment scope mapping (prod/test/DR) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Establish change-control enforcement: documentation update + risk delta note requirement in release/change workflow; define checks to prevent security-relevant releases without updated/approved documentation | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Develop and deliver role-based training packs (Administrators/engineers; Change managers/release operators) mapped to the documentation, including “Do/Do not” guidance for at least two features per component and completion evidence capture | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 28h | £2,500 |
| Run training sessions, collect completion evidence, and perform an audit-readiness validation (can personnel locate latest approved guidance; documentation-to-training version mapping; audit trail completeness) | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 192h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £5,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set the official documentation templates for identity services, logging, access control, and encryption services, including the risks of misuse or incorrect configuration.
- [ ] Create the first version-controlled documentation set for the on-premises system components listed in `sa-08.32_odp`, and assign named owners and review dates.
- [ ] Link each documentation section to the system’s configuration “source of truth” records for the relevant component and environment.
- [ ] Update the change control process so that, whenever identity, logging, access, or encryption settings are changed, the documentation is updated and a note is added explaining the change in risk (a “risk delta” note).
- [ ] Create and deliver role-based training materials that match the documentation. For each component, include “do” and “do not” guidance for at least two security-relevant features.
- [ ] Set up a way to record proof that training has been completed, and link each record to the correct document version. Also check that staff can find and access the most recent approved guidance.


---

#### SA-8.33 — Minimization (Enhancement)

This requirement is about collecting and using people’s personal details only when you genuinely need them, sharing only the minimum needed, and keeping them for no longer than necessary. Without this, organisations can unintentionally collect too much information, use it for the wrong reasons, share it with the wrong people, or keep it indefinitely. This increases the risk of privacy harm, complaints, regulatory action, and expensive clean-up after mistakes.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must have written privacy minimisation procedures that clearly set out what personal data may be collected, used, shared, and kept only when it is directly needed for authorised purposes. The procedures must also explain what to do when personal data is not needed.

The organisation must build these minimisation rules into system design and settings, document how they are applied, assess privacy impact and risks, assign clear responsibilities to the relevant staff and system developers, enforce the rules using practical controls, and review minimisation when systems or services are bought or changed, keeping evidence of this in the organisation’s records.

##### Privacy minimisation procedures and enforcement in app data flows

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define minimisation procedures (authorised-purpose driven) covering collection, use, sharing, and retention; include field-level rules, permitted recipients, and retention/deletion actions | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Create and maintain PII field inventory and purpose catalogue (forms, APIs, payloads, logs, exports, DB tables/columns); include necessity rationale and mapping to minimisation procedures | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Establish enforcement requirements and evidence standards for minimisation (field allowlists for collection/outbound sharing, log redaction/masking rules, retention window alignment, deletion/archival evidence) | Security Architect | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Produce change management and governance workflow updates: require minimisation procedure version reference and authorised-purpose linkage for schema/API/data-flow/retention changes; define required evidence artefacts | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Perform privacy impact assessment (or equivalent privacy risk assessment) for each authorised purpose and for major changes; explicitly assess necessity of each PII field, sharing scope, and retention duration | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Conduct control walkthroughs and audit-readiness review (evidence mapping to procedures, inventory, change records, and PIA outcomes); produce an audit pack for SA-8(33) enhancement | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Train relevant stakeholders (product/app owners, engineering, governance/change managers) on minimisation procedures, how to request/approve purpose changes, and how to produce required evidence | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 240h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Draft privacy minimisation procedures that set out the authorised reasons for collecting personal information (PII) and the specific PII that is allowed to be collected, used, shared, and kept for retention.
- [ ] Create and keep an auditable record of all personal data (PII) fields, showing which authorised purposes each one supports and why collecting each field is necessary.
- [ ] Set up application checks for input validation and clear application programming interface (API) rules so that only the required personal information (PII) fields are collected for each specific purpose.
- [ ] Set up field-by-field allowlists for outbound sharing integrations, and make sure logs and telemetry mask or remove any unnecessary personal data (PII).
- [ ] Set up and document storage retention controls—such as time-to-live (TTL), lifecycle rules, and deletion jobs—so data is kept only for the minimisation retention time windows.
- [ ] Update the change-management templates so that every change to data flows or data retention references the data minimisation procedure version and the supporting evidence.
- [ ] Carry out or update privacy impact assessments for each purpose or major change, and record the results of data minimisation (why it is needed, who it may be shared with, and how long it will be kept).


---

### SA-9 — External System Services (Control)

This requirement is about making sure that when you use outside companies to run services for you, they protect your information and your customers’ privacy to the same standard you would expect from your own teams. Without this, an external provider could allow the wrong people to access systems, respond too slowly to incidents, leave security weaknesses unaddressed, set up services incorrectly, keep poor records of activity, or handle data in ways that break privacy commitments—putting your organisation at risk even though you do not manage their day-to-day work directly.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set out in contracts that every provider must use strong safeguards, including access controls, incident handling, fixing weaknesses, secure configuration settings, recording of activity, encryption, privacy compliance, and ongoing monitoring. The organisation must also clearly document who is responsible for overseeing these services and what access users and staff have. It must then continuously check that providers are complying by using quarterly independent reports, annual independent assessments, regular reviews of service-level agreements, ongoing monitoring of provider alerts and logs, and tracked follow-up actions until any issues are fully resolved.

##### External provider security addendum with evidence rights & SLA remedies

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Create “Provider Security & Privacy Requirements” catalogue mapped to external-service control expectations (access control, incident response, vulnerability management, secure configuration, audit logging, encryption, privacy obligations, continuous monitoring) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Draft standard “External System Services Security & Privacy Addendum” template including: service boundaries, data handling, roles/responsibilities, evidence cadence, telemetry/log delivery requirements, measurable SLA outcomes, remedies/termination/transition assistance clauses | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Define evidence review criteria and acceptance thresholds (quarterly SOC 2 Type II / ISO 27001 reports and annual independent assessments), including remediation evidence requirements and escalation triggers | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Specify continuous monitoring telemetry contract requirements (SIEM-compatible log formats, alerting/notification mechanisms, API/webhook options, access method, retention expectations, and operational availability) and produce an implementation guidance pack for service owners | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Establish contract governance workflow and approval gates to ensure no external services contract is approved without the mandated addendum (or documented deviation with risk acceptance), including workflow artefacts and checklists | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement auditable “trust relationship record set” structure per provider (versioned addendum, requirements catalogue version, evidence received/reviewed, SLA review outcomes, telemetry access details, remediation tracking with closure evidence) and provide a template for operational use | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Train Procurement/Legal, Service Owners/Vendor Managers, and Security/Privacy reviewers on the addendum, evidence review, SLA remedies, and record-keeping; run a pilot with 2–3 active providers to validate operability and refine clauses | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 232h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a “Provider Security and Privacy Requirements” catalogue that links each required external service control to the relevant requirement, covering: access control, incident response, vulnerability management, secure configuration, audit logging, encryption, privacy compliance, and continuous monitoring.
- [ ] Publish a standard “External System Services Security and Privacy Addendum” template that includes: evidence rights, the responsibilities of end users and service providers, and the service-level agreement (SLA) remedies and response requirements.
- [ ] Add quarterly evidence submission requirements for the Service Organisation Control 2 (SOC 2) and International Organization for Standardization 27001 (ISO 27001) assessments, and include the requirement for an independent annual assessment, in the addendum.
- [ ] Add contractual requirements for continuous monitoring data (for example, logs compatible with security information and event management (SIEM) and/or alert notification mechanisms) that are sufficient to support compliance monitoring under the provider’s control requirements.
- [ ] Set measurable service level agreement (SLA) targets, broken down by severity, for patching and fixing vulnerabilities, responding to incidents, encryption, audit logging, and how quickly alerts and notifications are sent.
- [ ] Set up a contract approval checkpoint so that no external services contract can be approved unless the addendum is included and any agreed exceptions are documented.
- [ ] Set up and keep a complete, auditable record of the trust relationship for each provider. This should include evidence reviews, the results of service-level agreement (SLA) reviews, and tracking of any required fixes, with proof when each issue is closed.

#### SA-9.1 — Risk Assessments and Organizational Approvals (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the organisation considers security risks carefully before paying a third party to run or provide security services, and only moves forward when the right senior decision-makers have approved it. Without this, the organisation could end up outsourcing security work to a provider that creates new problems for the business, such as weaknesses attackers could exploit, mishandling personal information, disruption to important services, or hidden reliance on other companies in the provider’s supply chain.

To meet this expectation, before buying or outsourcing dedicated security services (for example, operating security tools, monitoring and responding to incidents, or providing key security services), the organisation must complete a written risk assessment. This assessment must cover: impact on business or mission, security risk, privacy risk, system risk, and supply-chain risk. The organisation must then obtain approval from the Chief Information Security Officer and the Contracting Officer Representative before the contract is awarded or the outsourcing begins, and keep clear records showing that both approvals and the risk assessment were completed on time.

- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define “dedicated information security services” scope criteria and procurement tagging rules (e.g., SOC monitoring/analysis/response, managed firewall operations, key management operations) and map to procurement categories/fields | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Produce the structured organisational risk assessment template (mandatory sections for mission/business, security, privacy, system, supply-chain; include service start date and contract award/commitment date fields) and publish as a controlled document | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure procurement workflow gates in the procurement/contracting system: (1) block PO release/signature until risk assessment artefact exists and is dated prior to award/outsourcing start; (2) enforce dual-approval requirement | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Implement workflow validation logic and audit logging (timestamped evidence of risk assessment completion, approval identities, and decision outcomes) including exception handling and escalation routes | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Configure evidence pack generation and retention in the acquisition file repository (auto-link risk assessment, contract/PO artefact, both approvals, service start date, award/commitment date) with retention/audit access controls | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £4,000 |
| Establish governance and operating procedures: roles/responsibilities (CISO, COR, risk owner, procurement ops), training for requesters, and periodic audit sampling process to verify gate effectiveness | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Run end-to-end pilot with 2–3 representative outsourced security service procurements; remediate workflow/template gaps and confirm acceptance criteria via audit evidence review | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 180h |  |
|---|---:|---:|
| Total Estimated Cost |  | £18,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set up the procurement process to identify and flag purchases or outsourcing of dedicated information security services.
- [ ] Create a written risk assessment template with required sections covering mission or business risks, security risks, privacy risks, system risks, and supply-chain risks.
- [ ] Put in place checks for workflow policy to stop any contract award or purchase order release unless the risk assessment is included and dated before the start of the award or outsourcing.
- [ ] Require two documented approvals before signing or making a commitment: one from the Chief Information Security Officer (CISO) and one from the Contracting Officer Representative (COR).
- [ ] Automate the creation of an auditable evidence pack that links the risk assessment, the contract or purchase order, the identities of the approvers, and the relevant dates.
- [ ] Save the evidence pack in the acquisition file repository and check that it can be retrieved when needed for an audit.
