#### SA-9.2 — Identification of Functions, Ports, Protocols, and Services (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure every external provider of managed services clearly explains, in writing, exactly how their service connects and works. This includes what the service does, which specific access points it uses, what communication rules it follows, and any supporting services it depends on.  

This matters because if these details are unclear or missing, the organisation could accidentally allow the wrong connections, find it difficult to block unsafe traffic, or be unable to explain and manage what is actually being used. That can lead to avoidable risk of disruption, data loss, or unauthorised access.  

To meet this requirement, the organisation must ask providers of cloud and on-premises managed services—including virtual private networks (VPNs), domain name system (DNS), email, web hosting, application programming interface (API) gateways, and third-party remote access—to provide a written, service-specific list before or at the start of using the service. The organisation must then record and keep this information in its procurement and oversight records, ensure it is included in contracts and service agreements and in the buying documents, and check that it matches the organisation’s security requirements.

##### Contractual Technical Appendix for vendor service ports/protocols

- Category: Manual
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the standard “Technical Appendix – Service Connectivity & Dependencies” schema (minimum required fields: functions, ports, protocols, other required services/components, scope mapping, environment applicability, version/change metadata) | Security Architecture Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Update procurement/contract templates for all in-scope external managed services to include the mandatory appendix schedule and acceptance language (incl. explicit requirement for ports/protocols) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure contract lifecycle workflow gate (e.g., CLM/contract approval process) to block approval unless appendix is present and passes minimum completeness checks (ports + protocols + service mapping) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | £3,000 |
| Create controlled repository guidance and linking model (how appendices are stored, versioned, and linked to vendor/service record and service oversight artefacts for audit traceability) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Develop appendix validation checklist and evidence pack for audit readiness (what “good” looks like; examples; required mapping granularity; management vs data plane expectations) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Train procurement/commercial, security architecture reviewers, and service owners on the appendix requirements, workflow gate, and how to handle provider updates/change notifications | Project Manager | Enterprise | 12h | £2,000 |
| Pilot the approach with 2–3 representative external services (e.g., managed DNS/email/API gateway/remote access), validate completeness, and refine templates/checks based on findings | Service Delivery Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 124h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £5,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Update procurement and contract templates to include a mandatory schedule titled **“Technical Appendix – Service Connectivity & Dependencies”** for all in-scope external managed services.
- [ ] Define and publish an internal appendix template that requires clear, explicit entries for each service’s functions, network ports (port numbers and endpoints), protocols (names and variants), and any other required services or components, with each entry linked to the specific service.
- [ ] Set up a contract lifecycle workflow “gate” that stops approvals unless the appendix is included, and ensure the required network ports and protocols are provided before or at the start of the service.
- [ ] Require providers to include management-plane and data-plane connectivity details (where applicable) in the appendix, rather than using generic descriptions.
- [ ] Store the completed appendix in a controlled, version-controlled repository. Link it to the relevant vendor or service record and to the related service oversight documents.
- [ ] Add a contractual change-notification clause that requires submitting an updated appendix whenever functions, ports, protocols, or required services are changed.

#### SA-9.3 — Establish and Maintain Trust Relationship with Providers (Enhancement)

This expectation is about being able to rely on external suppliers, not just on what they say, but on written commitments you can check. Without this, a supplier could fail to protect your systems and data, conceal weaknesses, ignore the security settings you agreed, or delay telling you about a security incident—leaving you exposed to financial loss, service disruption, regulatory issues, and harm to people’s personal information.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must, before and throughout the use of each external service provider, set out and document the trust requirements in contracts or service agreements. This includes providing evidence that required security standards are met (CMMC Level 2 and Level 3 evidence), allowing audit rights, supporting ongoing security monitoring, following the agreed secure configuration baseline, and reporting any security incident within 24 hours.

Where relevant, the contracts must also cover regulated handling and vulnerability management, and privacy obligations such as data minimisation, a lawful basis for processing, breach notification within 72 hours, and limiting access to personal data to only what is needed.

The organisation must keep the relevant records showing these trust arrangements are in place and continue to be maintained.

##### Provider trust clause pack with evidence gates and incident timelines

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Draft the “Trust Clause Pack” (contract/SLAs) covering sa-9.3_prm_1 trust requirements: CMMC-L2/L3 evidence, audit rights, continuous monitoring support, secure configuration baselines, and 24-hour incident reporting | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Produce annex templates for (1) minimum incident-notification trigger/channel/content (within 24 hours) and (2) secure configuration baseline requirements (versioned baseline, change notification expectations, evidence outputs) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Produce annex templates for (3) continuous monitoring support (monitoring outputs, frequency, evidence delivery mechanism) and (4) audit rights (authorised representatives, evidence access, remediation verification) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define the evidence pack structure and mapping method (clause pack → evidence requirements), including evidence freshness rules, acceptance criteria, and sign-off workflow for go-live gating | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Operationalise the acquisition trust gate in procurement/vendor management: update vendor onboarding workflow, enforce “no go-live without evidence review sign-off”, and maintain a provider trust register | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish ongoing trust maintenance procedures: periodic evidence refresh cadence, baseline change review process, monitoring output review, and documented review outcomes stored for audit readiness | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Create incident timeline and validation approach: define how provider incident notifications are recorded, how 24-hour expectations are tested (tabletop/test where feasible), and how outcomes feed continuous improvement | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 136h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Draft and get approval for a standard Trust Clause Pack that directly covers sa-9.3_prm_1, including evidence for CMMC Level 2 and Level 3, audit rights, support for continuous monitoring, secure configuration baseline settings, and reporting of security incidents within 24 hours.
- [ ] Create templates for provider evidence packs and guidance on how to match evidence to each clause pack annex, including rules for how up-to-date the evidence must be.
- [ ] Add an “acquisition trust” approval step to the vendor onboarding process. This step must require security sign-off confirming that the required evidence is complete, up to date, and matches the contract requirements before the vendor can go live.
- [ ] Set out and document what starts an incident notification, which communication channels must be used, and the minimum information that must be included for reporting within 24 hours. Include these requirements in the contract annex.
- [ ] Set up a regular schedule to update evidence and notify changes so that continuous monitoring can be maintained and baseline compliance remains secure, and record the results in the provider trust register.
- [ ] Carry out a contractual enforceability review (Legal and Compliance) to make sure audit rights and the obligation to provide evidence are clearly stated and can be followed in practice.


---

#### SA-9.4 — Consistent Interests of Consumers and Providers (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure that when you use external firms to manage your on-site technology and operational systems, their staff and working practices genuinely align with your organisation’s interests. If they do not, a provider could supply unsuitable staff, conceal who really owns the business, use subcontractors that you have not approved, or act in ways that put your organisation at risk—even if the contract documents look correct.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must first clearly identify which external providers, and which categories of their staff, are covered. It must then carry out background checks on the selected people before they start work on your premises, and keep evidence that these checks were completed. Before awarding or continuing contracts, it must review records of ownership and subcontractors. It must use only providers with a proven record of successful prior work (or document an approved exception using an alternative assurance approach), and it must record why each provider is considered trustworthy.

Finally, the organisation must plan and carry out regular, periodic, unannounced visits to the providers’ sites, and keep records of what was checked and any issues found.

##### Provider trust onboarding with evidence-led access gating

- Priority: Critical

| Implement access gating logic (block/revoke on-prem access approvals and privileged provisioning until evidence is present and valid; enforce selected-personnel list and time-bound access windows) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | £40,000 |

**Total Estimated Cost:** £90,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and publish an approved external provider catalogue for on-premises information technology (IT), operational technology (OT), and supporting services, grouped into risk tiers.
- [ ] Define which provider personnel categories must undergo background checks and have privileged access restricted until approval.
- [ ] Set up a governance, risk and compliance (GRC) and workflow onboarding process that requires supporting evidence for background checks, identifying the responsible party and any subcontractors, and recording the basis for trust.
- [ ] Use policy-as-code to prevent on-premises and privileged access approval requests from being completed until the required evidence is available and up to date.
- [ ] Update the contract and service level agreement (SLA) templates to include rights for routine, periodic, unannounced facility visits and to set out the provider’s obligation to cooperate.
- [ ] Link onboarding approval records to the organisation’s identity provider to automatically set up time-limited access, tied to the evidence log.
- [ ] Set up an audit-ready evidence log that shows whether information has been changed, linking the service provider, staff involved, the time periods when access was allowed, and the results of verification checks.


---

#### SA-9.5 — Processing, Storage, and Service Location (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure your information, and the services that handle it, are only used in approved places—so it is never processed, stored, or sent from the wrong country. If you allow providers to use other locations, you may lose control over which laws apply, make it harder to investigate and respond to incidents, and increase the risk that sensitive or regulated information is handled in ways you are not authorised to support.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must restrict where information is processed, stored, and where system services run to the United Kingdom and the United States (including facilities controlled by the Department of Defense). It must only use specific hosting and processing locations that are clearly listed in its system plan and have been checked and approved by Legal and Compliance for the relevant export and certification obligations.

The organisation must build these location limits into procurement processes, tender documents, service agreements, and contracts with external providers. It must also keep evidence showing Legal and Compliance have validated each approved location, and it must regularly confirm ongoing compliance whenever providers or service arrangements change.

##### SSP-approved location register with legal/compliance sign-off gates

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the Approved Locations Register data model (system-scoped, per service category), including required fields (location identifiers, processing/storage/service type, effective dates, scope, evidence links, legal/compliance approver, exception references) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create the initial Approved Locations Register entries for UK and US (including DoD-controlled facilities), covering cloud regions, data-centre identifiers, tenancy/contracted footprints, backup/DR targets, and logging/SIEM forwarding endpoints | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish legal/compliance validation workflow and evidence pack template for ITAR/EAR and CMMC-L2/L3 (scope mapping, approver sign-off, effective date rules, audit trail requirements) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Perform legal/compliance sign-off for every register entry (ITAR/EAR and CMMC-L2/L3) and record signed evidence with approver identity, scope, and effective dates | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Embed register references into the SSP (restricted locations section) and update SSP text to map “UK/US only” to explicit enumerated register IDs, including versioning and audit-ready traceability | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define procurement/vendor management gate: contract/SLA and onboarding checklist requiring mapping to Approved Location Register IDs, plus rejection criteria for unapproved regions/facilities | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Define operational verification and change triggers: CMDB/service inventory tagging requirements (Approved Location Register ID), runtime configuration change trigger rules, and re-validation/SSP update requirements when providers/regions/data flows change | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 156h | Total Estimated Cost | £0 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish the system-specific register of approved locations for processing, storing, and providing services, using clear location identifiers for the United Kingdom and the United States (including facilities controlled by the United States Department of Defense).
- [ ] Get legal and compliance approval for every entry in the register that covers International Traffic in Arms Regulations (ITAR), Export Administration Regulations (EAR), and Cybersecurity Maturity Model Certification level 2 and level 3 (CMMC-L2 and CMMC-L3), and keep the approval evidence with the scope and effective dates.
- [ ] Update the system security plan (SSP) to point to the register and list the approved locations for processing, storage, and service delivery.
- [ ] Update procurement templates, tender documents, and service level agreements (SLAs) to require suppliers to map services to Approved Location Register (ALR) IDs, and to prohibit use of any locations that are not approved.
- [ ] Set up a change-management approval step so that any new or changed services cannot be approved unless every processing, storage, and service endpoint is linked to approved location identifiers.
- [ ] Set up change triggers for any changes to the provider region, subcontractor, or service plan that require re-checking (re-validation) and updating the security service plan (SSP) before anything is used in production.


---

#### SA-9.6 — Organization-controlled Cryptographic Keys (Enhancement)

This expectation is about keeping the secret “scrambling codes” (encryption keys) for your protected information firmly under your control, even if you use an external supplier or outside service to store or move your data. If the supplier’s staff can access or use these keys, they could potentially remove the protection and read your confidential information. This could result in financial loss, legal issues, and damage to trust.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly identify which outside systems handle your encrypted data. It must then set things up so that only the organisation can encrypt and decrypt the data. This can be done by encrypting before sending and decrypting after receiving within the organisation, or by using an external component that still cannot reveal or use the keys.

The organisation must document its approach, include the requirement in purchasing rules, procedures, contracts, requests for proposals, and service agreements, and assign named responsibilities for managing encryption keys and managing suppliers. It must also be able to show—using evidence and testing—that supplier staff cannot decrypt the data.

##### Exclusive key control via organisation-side encryption/decryption

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| In-scope external systems and data-flow mapping: identify all storage/transmission flows requiring ciphertext-only handling; produce a system-by-system encryption/decryption pattern register | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Crypto architecture design: define client-side vs gateway-side encryption patterns per flow, including threat model for provider access and decryption exclusivity requirements | Security Architect | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Key management implementation plan: specify KMS/HSM key hierarchy, key usage policies, rotation, environment separation (prod/test/DR), and decrypt authorisation model (organisation-only identities/endpoints) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 28h | — |
| Implement encryption/decryption services and integration: configure organisation-side encryption at egress and decrypt at ingress using organisation-controlled keys; ensure external systems only receive/hold ciphertext | Platform Engineer | Department | 56h | £12,000 |
| Enforce exclusivity technically: remove/disable any provider support decryption pathways; implement least-privilege decrypt permissions, strong authentication for decrypt callers, and block plaintext export/escrow | Security Engineer | Department | 40h | £6,000 |
| Contract/SLA and operational controls: update procurement terms to prohibit provider key access/plaintext handling; add audit rights, evidence requirements, and remediation obligations | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Audit-ready evidence and verification testing: produce design/security documentation, run controlled tests proving provider-accessible paths cannot decrypt, and store results for assurance | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £3,500 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 232h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £21,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep an up-to-date, authoritative list of external systems that store or send encrypted organisation data.
- [ ] Use encryption on the client side or at the gateway so external systems only receive and store encrypted data (ciphertext).
- [ ] Set up organisation-managed key management service (KMS) and hardware security module (HSM) keys, and limit decryption (decrypt) actions to service identities controlled by the organisation.
- [ ] Disable or block any provider-accessible decryption, key-escrow, or support decryption routes, and document this control.
- [ ] Update procurement documents, contracts, and service level agreements (SLAs) to require that the provider’s staff cannot access encryption keys or plaintext data.
- [ ] Run and record verification tests to prove that paths accessible to the provider cannot decrypt, while paths accessible to the organisation succeed.


---

#### SA-9.7 — Organization-controlled Integrity Checking (Enhancement)

This requirement is about being able to confirm that information stored with an outside supplier stays complete and unchanged. Without this, data could be accidentally damaged or deliberately altered, and you might not find out until it is too late—leading to incorrect decisions, financial loss, or regulatory issues.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must ensure its systems can check the integrity of stored information while it remains in the supplier’s environment. This should use built-in checking methods that do not require moving or exporting the data. The organisation must also have clear, documented procedures for how these checks are carried out, name specific people responsible for integrity checking, and ensure that purchasing decisions include these needs. These requirements must be written into contracts, service agreements, and procurement documents so suppliers are required to cooperate.

The organisation’s plans for system security and supplier risk must also explain how integrity checking will be carried out for information stored externally.

##### External storage integrity verification via provider attestations

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

| Provider requirements pack: update procurement/SOW/contract clauses and technical interface requirements for signed attestations or challenge/response digests without exporting data | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Select and validate provider verification mechanism(s) for target storage services (technical workshops, API/endpoint validation, signature/attestation format confirmation) | System Design Authority | Business Unit | 24h | £8,000 |
| Build integrity-check service (workload identity integration, provider verification client, attestation/digest validation, expected-metadata comparison, mismatch classification) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 80h | £12,000 |
| Implement evidence capture and SIEM/logging integration (immutable log fields, correlation IDs, verification outcomes, signature validation results, audit-ready retention) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Operationalise checks (cadence scheduler, alerting/escalation workflows, runbooks, incident linkage triggers, and quarantine/recovery decision hooks) | Operations Lead | Department | 32h | — |
| Security & compliance assurance (threat model, security testing, key/certificate trust validation, documentation for system security plan and supplier management evidence) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | £5,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 256h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £31,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the data integrity checks for each external dataset (hash, Merkle root, and signed manifest) and set how often the checks are repeated (verification cadence).
- [ ] Update procurement documents and service level agreements (SLAs) to require the provider to prove their integrity, without exporting any data (for example, using an application programming interface (API) or a signed attestation/challenge-response).
- [ ] Set up an organisation integrity-check service that logs in to the provider and verifies the signed proof (attestations) and digital fingerprints (digests).
- [ ] Store the expected integrity information in a repository that is controlled by your organisation and access-restricted, and protect it using suitable integrity safeguards.
- [ ] Set up automated scheduled checks and alerts for any mismatches in the security information and event management (SIEM) or monitoring system.
- [ ] Document and train staff on procedures for running integrity checks, keeping evidence, and escalating any mismatches or incidents.
- [ ] Assign named responsibilities for choosing datasets, running the verification checks, and reviewing the evidence

#### SA-9.8 — Processing and Storage Location — U.S. Jurisdiction (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping your organisation’s information processing and data storage physically within the United States, so it only happens in facilities located within the United States’ legal jurisdiction. The real-world risk it helps prevent is that sensitive business information could be handled or stored in other countries, where you may have less control, fewer protections, and fewer legal options if something goes wrong—including unauthorised access or disruptive security incidents that could harm people, your operations, and other organisations.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define a “United States only” location rule and build it into how it buys and manages systems and services, including services provided by third parties. It must specify which information and services are covered, set clear requirements for external providers, and ensure these rules are included in procurement documents, contracts, and service agreements.

The organisation must also document how it decides which legal jurisdiction limits apply, and name specific people who are responsible for ensuring the rule is followed—from purchasing through to day-to-day use.

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Publish a United States–only jurisdiction standard that defines which information processing and data storage activities are in scope.
- [ ] For each acquisition, create a process to check whether the supplier processes and/or stores in-scope information, and confirm which jurisdictions apply.
- [ ] Set up an unavoidable procurement checkpoint that requires the jurisdiction review to be completed before any contract can be awarded.
- [ ] Update the standard contract and service level agreement (SLA) templates to require processing and storage only in the United States, restrict subcontractors, and include audit and attestation requirements.
- [ ] At onboarding and renewal, require and keep proof from the provider, including a signed statement confirming their residency and jurisdiction, a list of sub-processors, and a confirmation that services are provided from the United States region.
- [ ] Assign responsibility (RACI) for procurement approval gates, information security sign-off, and third-party risk monitoring, including documented steps for handling exceptions.

### SA-10 — Developer Configuration Management (Control)

This requirement ensures that every change to a system is properly controlled, recorded, and checked for safety and privacy impacts—starting when the system is first built and continuing through everyday use. Without this, weaknesses could be introduced without being noticed, fixes might be missed or only partly completed, and unauthorised or accidental changes could end up in the live system. This could result in data loss, disruption to services, or privacy breaches.

To meet this requirement, the system developer must keep a controlled, documented record of changes for the system’s key building parts. This includes the formal design, design documents, implementation records, source code, hardware diagrams, test set-ups, and the version currently in use. Only changes approved by the organisation may be made. Every approved change must be logged, including its potential security and privacy impacts.

The developer must also track any security weaknesses found, record how each one is addressed, and report the findings and results to the system security officer and the incident response lead.

##### Gated developer change control with approved artefact integrity

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define Configuration Items (CIs) and CI-to-repository/artifact-store mapping (formal model, design specs, implementation docs, source, schematics, test fixtures, signed release packages/images, SBOM/provenance artefacts) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement auditable change workflow in the ticketing system for security-relevant changes (mandatory fields: affected CIs, security impact, privacy impact, authorisation evidence, rollback/verification evidence; enforce approval record linkage) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Configure CI/CD gating to allow merges/builds/releases only when pipeline can validate linkage to an approved change record (change ID in commit metadata; pipeline verification; block non-compliant releases) | DevOps Lead | Department | 56h | £12,000 |
| Implement master copy and release artefact integrity controls (restrict write access to master branches/stores; enable signed commits/artifacts where supported; generate/retain checksums, SBOMs, and build provenance per release) | Security Engineer | Department | 48h | £15,000 |
| Build end-to-end security flaw traceability (flaw ticket → approved change(s) → release(s) → deployed version(s); define closure criteria with verification and deployment evidence) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement intended vs running version inventory and drift detection across environments (dev/test/prod/DR) with automated exception raising when running diverges from approved release record | Platform Engineer | Department | 40h | £8,000 |
| Reporting to System Security Officer and Incident Response Lead (event-driven + periodic reports: new flaws, resolutions with deployed versions, pipeline exceptions/drift findings; evidence pack generation for audits) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 304h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £41,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document the configuration items approved by the organisation, and link each one to the relevant repository or storage location (including the currently running compiled software).
- [ ] Set up a change process for all security-relevant changes that requires approval evidence and includes mandatory fields for both security impact and privacy impact.
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) so that code cannot be merged, built, or released unless the automated process confirms it is linked to an approved change record (change ID verification).
- [ ] Use integrity protections for master copies and release items (signed items, checksums, and provenance) and keep audit evidence for each release.
- [ ] Link vulnerability and security flaw tickets to the change process, so that each flaw is matched to the approved change(s) and to the software version(s) that have been deployed with the fix.
- [ ] Automatically record the software version running in each environment, and alert if it differs from the approved release record.
- [ ] Set up automated reports to the system security officer and the incident response lead showing the status of security flaws, the fixes applied, the software versions currently in use, and any changes that do not match the expected setup (including exceptions).

#### SA-10.1 — Software and Firmware Integrity Verification (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that every piece of software and firmware you receive from a supplier includes a way to prove it has not been secretly changed. Without this, unauthorised changes could be introduced without being noticed, which could cause systems to malfunction, leak information, or be taken over. It also helps prevent counterfeit parts being supplied as if they were genuine.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must require in procurement and supplier agreements that the developer enables integrity checking for all delivered software and firmware, including any later updates. The developer must also provide the information and the checking method you need to verify what you received.

You should keep clear records showing that the supplier-enabled checks were actually used for the specific versions you received and for the updates you installed. You should also link these checks to the approved change paperwork, so you can trace what was verified and when.

##### Require developer integrity verification artefacts for software/firmware

- Priority: Critical

| Produce supplier-facing requirements and contract language updates (SOW/SLAs/order forms) covering: integrity verification enabled for all delivered components and updates; artefacts tied to exact versions/build IDs; delivery of public keys/certificates where signatures are used; counterfeiting/substitution detection expectations | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Update supplier onboarding and acceptance criteria (supplier checklist, evidence requirements, and escalation path for non-compliance) to ensure upstream providers deliver the artefact pack for every release/update | Project Manager | Business Unit | 12h | — |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an “Integrity Verification Artefact Pack” template for software and firmware releases and updates, including integrity checks such as file hashes and/or signed manifest files or packages.
- [ ] Update procurement documents (statement of work (SOW), service level agreements (SLAs), and order terms) to require that every delivered component and every update includes integrity checks enabled by the developer.
- [ ] Require suppliers to provide integrity information linked to the exact component version and build identifier, and to include the required public keys or certificates whenever digital signatures are used.
- [ ] Set up a release intake acceptance checklist to confirm that the delivered files match the integrity information (or method) provided by the developer.
- [ ] Record the results of each verification (method used, software versions or build identifiers, whether it passed or failed, and the date and time) and link those results to the matching change or release approval in the change management system.
- [ ] Run a trial with one supplier’s release to confirm that the delivery package format and the checking process meet operational requirements before rolling it out more widely.

#### SA-10.2 — Alternative Configuration Management Processes (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that when changes are proposed to important systems or services, they are reviewed and approved by the organisation before anything is put into use, even if there is no dedicated development team managing those changes. Without this, risky changes or updates that could harm privacy may be introduced, which could lead to service disruption, exposure of sensitive information, or legal and reputational damage.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must put in place an alternative change-management process that uses suitable internal staff to review and approve every proposed change. This must include separate checks by people responsible for security and, where relevant, privacy. No change should be implemented until the required security and privacy impact assessments have been completed and recorded. The organisation must also document how this will work in its change-management policy and plan, clearly setting out roles and responsibilities, and keeping evidence of approvals and completed assessments for each change.

##### Three-gate alternate CM approvals for system/service changes

- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---|---:|---:|

| Define workflow gate requirements and acceptance criteria for CM gate, Security gate, and conditional Privacy gate (including required artefacts, evidence fields, and decision records) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure change/ticketing workflow with mandatory gate transitions (CM approval → Security approval → Privacy approval where applicable → Implementation/Release) and enforce required attachments/fields | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Implement policy-as-code / workflow validation rules to block transitions when required evidence is missing (e.g., affected configuration item identifiers, baseline mapping, data classification tags triggering privacy review) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | £8,000 |
| Operationalise reviewer independence and role mapping: create/confirm organisational reviewer groups/roles, ensure approvers are not change initiators, and document escalation paths for gate resolution | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Produce audit-ready evidence templates and run a pilot across representative change types (enterprise application config, infrastructure config, COTS/service updates), then remediate gaps found in pilot evidence and ordering | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 24h | — |
| Deliver training and rollout communications for Change Managers/Service Owners and gate reviewers; confirm adoption for both manual and CI-driven releases | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 152h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £14,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Update the configuration management policy and configuration management plan to define the SA-10(2) alternative configuration management process for situations where there is “no dedicated developer configuration management team”.
- [ ] Set up the change or ticket workflow so that **Change Management (CM)** and **Security** approval are always required, and **Privacy** approval is required only when the change affects privacy.
- [ ] Define the required ticket information for each approval stage: the change management (CM) approval record, the security impact analysis, and the privacy impact analysis where personal data is in scope.
- [ ] Set up workflow controls so that a task cannot be moved to “implemented/released” until all required approvals and supporting analyses are attached and have been reviewed.
- [ ] Assign independent review groups or roles for configuration management (CM), security, and privacy, and document what each group or role is responsible for.
- [ ] Run a short pilot using the latest system or service and any approved changes to the commercial off-the-shelf (COTS) configuration, and check that the audit records show that all required approvals and assessments were completed before the changes were put into place.

#### SA-10.3 — Hardware Integrity Verification (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the hardware you buy and receive can be checked to confirm it has not been secretly changed before it reaches you. Without this, someone could swap parts or tamper with the device or its software, and you might only find out after it has caused disruption, data loss, or financial harm.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must require the supplier or developer to provide and enable a practical way to verify the hardware’s integrity using their own checking methods and tools. This can include hard-to-copy identifiers, verifiable serial numbers, and physical protections that show if tampering has occurred. You must also make sure the same verification approach applies to any hardware and firmware updates delivered as part of the service.

Finally, you should keep evidence that these checks were actually carried out for the items and updates you receive, and that the same approach remains in place for later changes.

##### Developer-enabled hardware integrity checks for deliveries and updates

- Priority: High

| Define acceptance criteria and PASS/FAIL recording requirements (including linkage to asset records, component identity, and update/change/release identifiers) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create procurement/contract clause pack embedding SA-10(3) IVA enablement, update coverage, evidence-pack delivery, and developer tool/procedure obligations | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Establish standard receiving/commissioning workflow (SOP) for executing IVA checks on arrival/installation and for verifying authenticity of delivered firmware/hardware updates | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure evidence capture in the configuration/change management repository (IVA versioning, delivery/commissioning verification records, update verification records, retention tagging) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Train receiving/commissioning and change/release stakeholders on the IVA template, workflow, and evidence handling (including escalation paths for FAIL outcomes) | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Pilot the end-to-end process with one representative hardware component family and one update release; remediate gaps and finalise for rollout | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £3,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 176h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £3,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an Integrity Verification Approach (IVA) template that specifies, for each hardware component family: the required integrity-check mechanism(s), the verification steps to follow, and clear objective pass/fail criteria.
- [ ] Update the procurement and statement of work (SOW) contract clauses to require the developer to enable hardware integrity checks and to provide the organisation with the required tools and instructions.
- [ ] For every delivery and for every delivered hardware and firmware update, require an evidence pack that includes the verification results and the PASS/FAIL outcome, linked to the relevant asset and release or change identifiers.
- [ ] Create a receiving and commissioning acceptance checklist that carries out the independent verification and records evidence that is ready for audit.
- [ ] Ensure that change and release processes require verification evidence based on internal verification and approval (IVA) for any delivered firmware or hardware updates before they are accepted for operational use.
- [ ] Store internal vendor assurance (IVA) approval records and verification evidence in the organisation’s configuration and change management repository, and keep them for the period required by organisational retention policy.

#### SA-10.4 — Trusted Generation (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that when a developer creates a new version of the system’s key building blocks, they can show exactly what has changed by automatically comparing the new output with the previously approved version. Without this kind of checking, harmful or unintended changes could be introduced during development, which could mean the system no longer works as intended or that its built-in protections are weakened.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must require the system developer to use comparison tools to confirm that newly generated security-relevant hardware descriptions, source code, and object code match the earlier approved versions. In practice, the developer should be able to demonstrate that each new version of these items has been compared against what was approved before, so that any authorised updates continue to enforce the system’s security rules.

##### Trusted build gates using diffing of security-relevant artefacts

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define security-relevant artefact taxonomy and coverage list (hardware descriptions/equivalents, source, object/build outputs, build/config/security bundles) including classification rules and exclusions | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design trusted build gate workflow and promotion criteria (baseline linkage, authorised change record mapping, diff acceptance rules, failure handling, rollback expectations) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement CI/CD “trusted generation” stage to generate artefacts in a controlled build environment and capture artefact identifiers (commit/build IDs, hashes, signing/provenance metadata) | DevOps Lead | Department | 56h | — |
| Integrate automated diff/comparison tooling per artefact type (text/AST-aware diffs for source/config; hash/binary diff for object outputs) and produce machine-readable diff evidence | Security Engineer | Department | 48h | £6,000 |
| Implement promotion gate enforcement in pipeline (block promotion on unauthorised diffs; allow promotion only when diffs are empty or match an approved baseline update/change record) | Operations Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Establish audit-ready append-only evidence storage and retention (immutable log storage, evidence schema, reproducibility pointers, access controls) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | £3,000 |
| Baseline repository management and release-line governance (baseline versioning, review workflow, linkage to change records, periodic baseline refresh process) | Build/Release Manager | Business Unit | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 256h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £9,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and record which items (“artefacts”) in your delivery pipeline are security-relevant for this application, such as hardware descriptions, source code, and compiled (object) code.
- [ ] Create and keep an approved “baseline” repository for each release line, for every type of security-relevant artefact.
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipeline steps that create new deliverables and automatically compare them against the approved baseline versions.
- [ ] Set up “promotion gates” so a release is blocked unless the changes are either empty or exactly match a change record that has been explicitly authorised.
- [ ] For each build, capture and store audit evidence, including the baseline reference, the new artefact identifiers, the comparison results (differences) and hashes, and the build history and signing details.
- [ ] Review and test the workflow using at least one authorised change and one simulated unauthorised change to confirm that the access gate controls are enforced.


---

#### SA-10.5 — Mapping Integrity for Version Control (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the organisation’s “master version” records for important parts of the system stay exactly the same between what the developer builds and what the organisation keeps on site. In everyday terms, it stops the documentation and the real system from drifting apart. If they do drift, the organisation may unknowingly use the wrong software, firmware, or hardware designs, which can cause outages, failed updates, or hidden weaknesses that are difficult to spot and fix.

To meet this expectation, the system developer must:
- Keep a documented link between the developer’s master build information and the on-site master copy for the currently approved version.
- Update that link whenever the current version changes.
- Check, item by item, that the two master records match for the current version during initial development and later updates.

The developer must also produce and keep clear evidence of these checks. This evidence must show the version, what was compared, the result, and that all relevant items were covered—including design information and source code identifiers—so the organisation can demonstrate compliance during reviews.

##### Signed version manifest and automated mapping reconciliation

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define canonical identifier schema (hardware/software/firmware/design/source-code/build IDs) and mapping rules, including version label conventions and normalisation/formatting requirements | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement version manifest generation in the developer build pipeline (complete item list, deterministic output, machine-readable format, and version metadata) | DevOps Lead | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Implement cryptographic signing and access-controlled storage for manifests (key management integration, signature verification metadata, audit logging) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Implement automated reconciliation service (signature validation, item-by-item comparison against on-site master copy, delta classification, and comparison report generation) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | £18,000 |
| Extend/align on-site master copy (CMDB/asset inventory + application/endpoint/config records) to use the canonical identifiers and current-version labelling; produce a “current version” dataset export for reconciliation | Infrastructure Lead | Department | 48h | — |
| Implement release/current-version approval gating (block compliance status when reconciliation fails; define workflow integration points and escalation path for deltas) | Service Delivery Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |
| Produce audit-ready evidence pack per current version (stored reconciliation results, timestamps, items checked, pass/fail outcome, and investigation-ready delta logs) and document operating procedures | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 296h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £24,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define a single, standard set of identifiers for all security-relevant hardware, software, firmware, designs and drawings, and source code and build records.
- [ ] Add a build-process step that creates a complete version manifest for every current release or update.
- [ ] Add a cryptographic signature to the manifest creation process, and store the signed manifests in a repository that only authorised users can access.
- [ ] Update the organisation’s on-site master records (configuration management database (CMDB) and inventory/configuration records) to use the same standard (canonical) identifiers and the current version labels.
- [ ] Set up an automated reconciliation job that checks the document signatures and compares each item one-by-one against the on-site master copy.
- [ ] Set up approval checks for the current release version so that approval is only granted after a reconciliation pass for that current version is completed.
- [ ] Keep the current version’s evidence for reconciliation and signature checks, including the list of items reviewed and the pass or fail result.


---

#### SA-10.6 — Trusted Distribution (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that any important update provided by a supplier is exactly the same as the approved version it was based on, with no changes made in secret along the way. Without this, an accidental or malicious change could be introduced into hardware, software, or firmware updates. That could cause systems to malfunction, expose sensitive information, or allow attackers to gain access through a “trusted” update.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must require the developer to use documented, repeatable steps for trusted delivery. These steps must be based on clearly identified approved master copies. The developer must check each update before sending it to confirm it matches the master copy exactly. The developer must also keep evidence showing these checks were completed, and must only deliver the update after it passes verification.

The organisation must also define in its purchasing documents which updates are considered security-relevant, set clear responsibilities in contracts and agreements, review and monitor the developer’s update handling over time, and keep records that link each delivered update to the approved master copy and the verification results.

##### Trusted update distribution with master-copy traceability evidence

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define and document scope of “security-relevant updates” (including examples for firmware/BIOS, signed installers, agent updates, container images, OS/app patches) and map to procurement/governance artefacts | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Update procurement/vendor management templates: contract/SLA clauses requiring master-copy maintenance, pre-release exact-match verification, controlled distribution endpoints, and per-delivery evidence contents | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define master-copy traceability evidence requirements and evidence schema (master copy ID/version, expected hash/signature values, release record reference, delivery confirmation, retention and access rules) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Establish organisation evidence intake and receipt verification workflow (controlled repository structure, intake checklist, receipt-side verification steps, and documented rationale when independent verification is not feasible) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create release/operations runbook for trusted update distribution (handover steps from developer evidence to internal release record; controls preventing modification between verification and delivery; audit trail expectations) | Operations Lead | Department | 16h | — |
| Implement supplier governance and ongoing compliance monitoring (audit rights, SLA/KPI checks, periodic evidence review cadence, exception handling, and escalation paths) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Conduct pilot rollout for one representative update type (e.g., signed installer or agent update): validate end-to-end evidence completeness, traceability to receiving asset/release record, and independent verification feasibility | Project Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 140h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish a list of “security-relevant updates” to be included in procurement scope, covering firmware/basic input/output system (BIOS), signed installers, updates to installed agents, and container images.
- [ ] Update the tender and contract/service-level agreement (SLA) templates so that developers must keep the approved master versions under configuration management.
- [ ] Add contract clauses requiring that, before any release, each update is checked to ensure it exactly matches the corresponding master copy, and that it is released only after this verification succeeds.
- [ ] Use controlled distribution channels and packaging so that verified items cannot be changed between the time they are checked and when they are delivered.
- [ ] Set required evidence details for each delivery (master copy ID and version, expected hash or signature, the release record reference, and delivery confirmation), and set a deadline for when the evidence must be delivered.
- [ ] Set up a central place to collect evidence, and link each delivery’s evidence to the relevant receiving asset and release record so you can trace it for audit purposes.
- [ ] Where technically feasible, verify on receipt that the delivered item matches what the developer expected by comparing its hash or signature with the expected values provided by the developer.


---

#### SA-10.7 — Security and Privacy Representatives (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that the right experts approve important system changes before they are released to live (production) systems. This is important because live changes can unintentionally weaken security or mishandle people’s personal information, and fixing these problems after systems have been updated can be difficult and costly.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must include the Information System Security Officer in the formal change review and approval process for every approved production change to Confidential and Secret systems, so security risks are checked before the change is implemented.

In addition, the organisation must include the System Privacy Officer in the same review and approval process for every approved production change that affects the way personal data is moved or processed, so privacy impacts are considered before anything is released.

##### Gate CAB approvals with ISSO/SPO mandatory reviewers

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

| Design workflow gating logic and approval rules (conditional routing for Confidential/Secret → ISSO; personal data impact → SPO; both → both) including “no bypass” transitions to CAB-approved/ready for production | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Configure ITSM/change tooling: add structured intake fields (classification, personal-data impact, DPIA/artefact linkage) and enforce controlled-option selection + justification when personal-data impact = yes | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |

| Configure automatic audit evidence capture (store approver identity + timestamp + change ID/version for ISSO/SPO approvals; ensure evidence is retained with the SA-10b change record) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 136h

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Update the change request form to record the system classification and whether personal data is affected, using approved (controlled) options.
- [ ] Set up the SA-10b change workflow so that any production changes classified as **Confidential** or **Secret** require approval from the **Information System Security Officer (ISSO)**.
- [ ] Set up the SA-10b change workflow so that any production change that affects personal data flows or processing requires approval from the SPO.
- [ ] Add workflow validation rules to prevent moving a change to “change advisory board (CAB) approved” or “ready for production” when the required approvals are not in place.
- [ ] Enable automatic recording of the approver’s identity and the date and time for the information security service owner (ISSO) and service process owner (SPO) in the change advisory board (CAB) record.
- [ ] Set up scheduled reports to check whether any changes approved by the Change Advisory Board (CAB) are missing the required approvals from the Information System Security Officer (ISSO) and the Senior Procurement Officer (SPO). Send any gaps to the CAB process owner so they can be fixed through the CAB process.


---

### SA-11 — Developer Testing and Evaluation (Control)

This requirement is about making sure the people who build your software keep checking it for security and privacy problems long after the design is finished—not just once at the start. Without this, weaknesses could be introduced in new releases or after important changes, potentially leading to unauthorised access, data leaks, or harm to individuals’ personal information.

To meet this expectation, the developer must create and follow an ongoing plan for both security and privacy checks, and keep records showing the plan was carried out and what the results were. Every time code is released, and after any change that could affect security, they must run a full set of checks, including testing small parts, combined parts, and the whole system, as well as repeating checks to confirm nothing has broken. These repeated checks must happen at least monthly even if there is no release.

The checks must cover all parts that affect security and how they work together. They must use a combination of code review and real running tests, plus authorised attempts to find weaknesses. Any problems found must be recorded, tracked through a clear and verifiable process to fix them and confirm the fix worked, and then corrected.

##### CI/CD security & privacy quality gates with evidence and remediation

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Produce versioned Security & Privacy Assessment Plan template and initial plan (living artefact) covering static analysis, dynamic analysis, targeted penetration tests, and testing stages (unit/integration/system/regression) with required frequency and evidence outputs | Application/Software Engineering Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create and maintain auditable “security-relevant components & interfaces” register and map each entry to CI/CD test targets (including release/change traceability fields) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement CI/CD quality gates: release and security-change triggers; unit→integration→system→regression execution; monthly regression scheduler; promotion block rules based on evidence/remediation status | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Integrate static analysis, dependency/SBOM checks, and secret scanning into pipelines with standardised report formats and run-ID evidence capture | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £18,000 |
| Implement dynamic analysis (DAST) in ephemeral test environments and security-focused integration tests; ensure environment segregation and evidence retention per run | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £12,000 |
| Stand up targeted penetration testing capability for impacted interfaces (authorised/scoped), including orchestration hooks from CI/CD, test environment controls, and penetration test summary evidence | Security Testing Lead | Enterprise | 64h | £25,000 |
| Implement trackable remediation workflow: findings ingestion → issue creation with severity/component/interface → remediation ownership → retest/verification gates → closure with evidence; enforce “no promotion without closure/approved exception” | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Evidence management and audit readiness: store artefacts per run (reports/logs/summaries), link to release identifier and change record, apply access controls and retention aligned to policy | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 376h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £61,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a version-controlled Security and Privacy Assessment Plan that sets out the types of tests to be carried out, how deep they go, what areas they cover, how often they are repeated, and what proof (evidence documents) must be produced.
- [ ] Keep an auditable record of security-relevant components and interfaces, and link each one to the automated tests that cover it.
- [ ] Set up the continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipeline so that, every time code is released, it automatically runs unit tests, integration tests, system tests, and regression tests, and also runs them after any change that affects security.
- [ ] Run monthly regression tests in the pipeline, even if there is no release.
- [ ] Add static analysis, dynamic analysis, and targeted penetration tests (with a defined scope) to the pipeline quality checks.
- [ ] Set up a tracked process to fix security flaws, where each fix is retested and verified before the issue is marked as closed.
- [ ] Store and protect evidence for each pipeline run, and link the results to release identifiers and change records.


---

#### SA-11.1 — Static Code Analysis (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that, before software is added to your systems, the people writing the code use an automated tool to check it for common security weaknesses and then record what the tool finds. Without this, simple coding mistakes or old, vulnerable code can be missed and may slip into your systems. This could lead to unauthorised access, data loss, or service disruption, which could be costly and harm your organisation’s reputation.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must require the system, component, or service developer to run static code analysis on their source code to identify typical flaws, and to produce clear written results showing what the scan found. The developer must also provide those documented results as evidence that the analysis was carried out, so the organisation can review them and track whether any issues are addressed.

##### CI/CD static analysis with audit-ready reports and merge gates

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Select and standardise SAST + SCA tooling (including SARIF support) and define tool versions, rule sets/quality profiles, and scan scope per technology (e.g., Java/.NET/Node) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | £18,000 |
| Build CI/CD pipeline template with SAST + dependency analysis stages on every PR and before merge/release (including caching, timeouts, and fail-fast behaviour) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement audit-ready report generation: capture repo/commit/branch/PR/build metadata, tool name/version, scan timestamp; output machine-readable SARIF and human-readable summary; ensure consistent artefact naming | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Configure policy-as-code merge/release gates for critical/high findings and medium triage; implement suppression/acceptance workflow with expiry dates and mandatory rationale links | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement developer disposition workflow integration (fix links, suppression/acceptance records linked to PR/issue tracker) and ensure required fields are enforced in the pipeline | Software Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish immutable, access-controlled evidence retention for scan reports and metadata tied to build artefacts and release records (including retention period and access controls) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Create defect density and false-positive/suppression rate tracking dashboards and periodic review process (monthly/quarterly) with tuning actions logged | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 252h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £24,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Choose and standardise software security testing (SAST) and software composition analysis (SCA) tools for all application repositories.
- [ ] Add automated code checks (static analysis) to the continuous integration (CI) process so they run on every pull request and every release candidate.
- [ ] Set up the tools to produce consistent, audit-ready reports that include the commit identifier (commit SHA), the pull request or build reference, and the version of each tool.
- [ ] Set up automated “policy-as-code” checks at the point of merging and releasing code, so that releases are blocked when critical defect levels are exceeded or when there is increased risk from vulnerable software dependencies.
- [ ] Require developers to record what action is taken for each issue (a link to the fix, the reason for accepting the risk, or a suppression that expires).
- [ ] Store scan reports and their details in an unchangeable, access-controlled evidence repository, linked to the relevant build outputs.
- [ ] Set up regular reviews of defect density and the rates at which defects are suppressed or incorrectly flagged as false positives for the most critical defect categories.


---

#### SA-11.2 — Threat Modeling and Vulnerability Analyses (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure the people building a system think through, before and during testing, how the system could be attacked and what weaknesses might be hidden in both the overall design and the individual parts. Without this, changes made during development can accidentally introduce new problems, and attackers could take advantage of exposed connections, weak third-party components, or poorly designed login and permission rules. This could lead to data loss, service disruption, or unsafe outcomes—especially where office information technology (IT) is connected with operational technology (OT).

To meet this requirement, the organisation must ensure the system developer carries out threat thinking and checks for vulnerabilities during development and again during testing and evaluation. They must use the system’s impact level, any mixed IT/OT context, known or assumed threats, how data moves through the system, where responsibility and trust change between parties, and the level of risk the organisation is willing to accept.

The developer must:
- analyse every interface and data path that can be reached from outside the system
- assess all components and any third-party dependencies
- use recognised, structured methods to identify threats and standard severity ratings
- use both automated and manual testing approaches
- review the code and configuration
- provide clear written evidence of the threats found, weaknesses identified, risk ratings, planned fixes, and the final sign-off of any remaining risk by the Information System Security Officer.

##### Threat model & vuln analysis gates with STRIDE/CVSS evidence

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define/confirm threat-modelling & vulnerability analysis gate requirements (evidence fields, STRIDE scope rules, CVSS scoring approach, acceptance criteria, residual risk linkage to release) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create/maintain required threat-modelling context templates per release (impact level, data flows, trust boundaries, externally reachable interfaces, assumptions/known threats, mitigation/residual risk sections) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement STRIDE-based threat modelling workflow and evidence pack generation (system-level model + mapping to interfaces/data flows, attack paths/abuse cases, trust-boundary crossings, traceability to requirements) | Security Engineer | Department | 32h | — |
| Implement development-gate vulnerability analysis workflow (SAST + dependency scanning + configuration review), including CVSS-based triage and remediation tracking linked to the evidence pack | DevOps Lead | Department | 40h | £6,000 |
| Implement testing/evaluation-gate verification workflow (DAST + manual penetration testing scoping for externally reachable interfaces, remediation verification results, re-analysis evidence updates) | Security Engineer | Department | 48h | £18,000 |
| Configure CI/CD pipeline lifecycle gates (block progression to testing/evaluation unless evidence completeness is met, including ISSO residual risk sign-off artefact linkage to the release candidate) | Platform Engineer | Department | 32h | £4,000 |
| Establish ISSO residual risk sign-off process and audit-ready evidence linking (review checklist, sign-off capture, versioning, retention, and audit trail integrity) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 208h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £28,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish the information needed for threat modelling, including the impact level, any information about information technology (IT) and operational technology (OT), the known and assumed threats, the data flows, the trust boundaries, and the risk levels that are acceptable.
- [ ] Create threat-modelling templates based on STRIDE that require, for every externally accessible interface, documented routes an attacker could take (attack paths), examples of how the system could be misused (abuse cases), and where data or actions move across trust boundaries (trust-boundary crossings).
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) checks so that, during development, the system automatically runs static application security testing (SAST), scans for vulnerable dependencies, and reviews configuration changes. Use Common Vulnerability Scoring System (CVSS) scores to prioritise issues and keep records of triage decisions.
- [ ] Set up testing and assessment checkpoints to run dynamic application security testing (DAST). For externally accessible interfaces, require targeted manual penetration testing and record the affected software versions and the results of the checks.
- [ ] Set up evidence generation that creates audit-ready threat modelling and vulnerability assessment reports, showing how each finding links back to the original requirements and the documented mitigations.
- [ ] Before promoting a release to testing and evaluation, require that the remaining risk sign-off for ISSO is recorded and linked to the release deliverables.


---

#### SA-11.3 — Independent Verification of Assessment Plans and Evidence (Enhancement)

This requirement is about having an independent person double-check that the developer’s security and privacy testing plans were followed correctly, and that the evidence collected from that testing is both accurate and complete. Without this independent check, mistakes or gaps could be missed, which could leave weaknesses that others could exploit or privacy promises that are not actually met. This could harm customers, breach legal responsibilities, and damage trust.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must appoint an independent security assessor who was not involved in creating the security and privacy assessment plans or the supporting evidence. The assessor must report to the Chief Information Security Officer and have the right training and professional certifications for assessments. The organisation must then provide the assessor with enough information to carry out the verification. If any information is missing, the organisation must authorise the assessor to obtain what is needed to complete the checks for both security and privacy.

##### Independent IV&V gate for security/privacy assessment plans and evidence

- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define IV&V gate scope, independence criteria, and lifecycle triggers (e.g., pre-release, post-remediation, major change before production) including required verification depth and sampling approach | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Establish assessor qualification and independence evidence requirements (training/certification checks, conflict-of-interest declarations, reporting line to CISO) and maintain an auditable qualification record | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Appoint independent IV&V assessor(s) and complete independence validation (including documented confirmation of non-involvement in plan/evidence development) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 8h | — |

| Implement controlled access workflow for verification inputs (read-only evidence repository, time-bound access to supporting logs/artefacts, escalation/authority path for missing information) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
