| Produce auditable IV&V verification reports for each gate (what was reviewed, plan/evidence versions, evidence identifiers/hashes, method, gaps, pass/conditional/fail decision) and submit outcomes to the CISO with retention of records | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 136h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Appoint an independent assessor who meets the organisation’s defined independence requirements, and keep the qualification evidence.
- [ ] Define the entry and exit requirements for independent verification and validation (IV&V) gates, and set the key lifecycle milestones for verifying the security and privacy assessment plan.
- [ ] Create and enforce a standard “evidence pack” template that covers both the security and privacy assessment plans and the proof that those plans were carried out.
- [ ] Set up a read-only evidence workspace and give the assessor time-limited access to the supporting systems and logs they need.
- [ ] Set up an approved decision-maker and escalation route so the assessor can request any missing information needed to complete the verification.
- [ ] Require the assessor to produce an independently verifiable and validatable (IV&V) report that can be audited. The report must include: the versions of the plans and evidence that were reviewed, the identifiers and checksums (hashes) for the evidence, the method used to verify the work, and the final conclusion. Submit the report to the chief information security officer (CISO).


---

#### SA-11.4 — Manual Code Reviews (Enhancement)

This requirement is about having a careful human check of the most sensitive parts of the software before it is released. The goal is to confirm that the code works as intended and does not create opportunities for attackers. Without this, serious weaknesses could be missed—for example, incorrect checks for logins and permissions, mistakes in how secret keys and encryption are handled, or unsafe responses when the system receives unexpected inputs. These problems could lead to unauthorised access, data theft, or the compromise of the system.

The organisation must make sure the software developer keeps a documented list of the specific critical code areas that require manual review. The organisation must assign responsibility for reviewing these areas and carry out a peer review that checks the code against the organisation’s documented expectations for threats and its permission rules.

The reviewer must also confirm that encryption is implemented correctly, that inputs are checked properly, and that errors are handled safely. After the review, the reviewer must provide a recorded sign-off covering exactly the agreed scope that was reviewed.

The organisation must keep records showing what code areas were reviewed and what was approved.

##### Manual review gate for critical auth/access/crypto code in SDLC

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Establish critical-code inventory process and repository tagging approach (module/file/function granularity, CODEOWNERS/security labels, scope rules for auth/access/crypto/firmware) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define the manual review checklist aligned to threat model and access control matrix, including crypto correctness, input validation, error handling, and required sign-off fields | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement CI/CD gate logic to detect changes to tagged critical code and require completion of the checklist + recorded reviewer sign-off before merge/release (including firmware artefacts from delivery pipeline) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £3,000 |
| Configure evidence capture and audit trail (system of record linkage to change request; store checklist, reviewer identity, timestamps, reviewed artefact identifiers: commit/build/release version; ensure traceability) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | £2,500 |
| Define reviewer accountability and approval workflow (authorised reviewer list, required approvals, separation of duties rules, escalation path for missing/invalid sign-off) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Run pilot on a representative set of critical-code changes; validate gate behaviour, evidence completeness, and reviewer usability; remediate gaps and update procedures | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 24h | — |
| Produce operational runbook and training materials for developers/reviewers (how to perform review, how to complete checklist, how to satisfy evidence requirements, how to resolve gate failures) | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 160h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £5,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and keep up to date an inventory of the specific critical code that must be manually checked, including code related to authentication, access control, cryptography, and security-relevant firmware, down to the module and function level.
- [ ] Create a manual code review checklist that explicitly covers peer review of the threat model and access-control matrix, checks that cryptography is correct, verifies input validation, and reviews error handling.
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) so that code changes cannot be merged or released if they affect tagged critical code, unless there is completed checklist evidence and documented approval from the reviewer.
- [ ] Require that reviewer approval is recorded with the reviewer’s identity and linked to the exact item being approved (commit hash, build identifier, or release version).
- [ ] Keep and store manual code review records in an auditable system of record, with clear traceability back to the change request.


---

#### SA-11.5 — Penetration Testing (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure the people who build your system deliberately try to “break in” in a controlled way, so weaknesses are found before criminals do. Without this, problems in the parts of the system that users and administrators rely on—such as publicly available services, internal user and administrator functions, website features, and the ways systems connect and communicate with each other—could allow unauthorised access, access to higher-than-allowed privileges, or access to sensitive information. This could happen through weaknesses in login and session handling.

The organisation must require the system developer to carry out thorough penetration testing using both manual checks and automated checks. Testing must cover every service that can be reached from outside and every internal user and administrator function. The testing should also check whether protections for authentication and sessions can be bypassed, and what the potential impact could be, up to privilege escalation and unauthorised access to data.

Testing must only take place during pre-approved test windows. It must not disrupt operational technology processes, must stay within the agreed scope, and must ensure any personal data collected during testing is properly protected, kept to a minimum, and handled in line with privacy requirements. There must be a documented plan and the results must be reviewed independently.

##### Developer penetration testing contract with scope, depth, and OT-safe constraints

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Establish authoritative scope inventory for the system/component/service (externally reachable services + internally reachable user/admin supporting services), including authentication/IdP integration points, session/token mechanisms, privilege boundary surfaces, and environment segregation | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Draft and approve Penetration Testing Plan requirements (breadth, depth, methods, evidence expectations, and explicit OT-safe constraints including “no exploit beyond agreed scope” and approved test windows) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Update procurement/acquisition artefacts (SOW/SLA/contract clauses) to require: plan submission/approval pre-testing, scope-to-evidence traceability matrix, independent verification, remediation retesting, and privacy/data handling controls (minimisation, redaction, secure storage, retention limits, deletion/return attestation) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create scope-to-evidence traceability matrix template and acceptance criteria (inventory item → test case(s) → evidence artefacts → validated finding(s) → impact assessment), including rules for redaction/masking of any personal data | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Execute independent verification of plan completeness and coverage (review of breadth/depth mapping, method suitability, constraints/OT-safety controls, and evidence quality requirements) prior to any testing commencing | Cybersecurity testing lead / verifier | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Coordinate and govern penetration testing execution under approved windows (including test window scheduling, OT-safe change controls, monitoring/stop conditions, and ensuring no disruption to OT processes) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Validate and sign-off results: manual confirmation of findings beyond tool output, review of evidence package, completion of traceability matrix, and approval of remediation retesting requirements | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Perform remediation retesting and privacy/data handling assurance (verify fixes, confirm re-test within agreed constraints/windows, and obtain deletion/return attestation for any captured personal data) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

Total Estimated Effort: **216 Hours**  
Total Estimated Cost: **£0**

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep an up-to-date, authoritative list of all services that can be reached from outside the organisation, and all internal user and administrator support services for the system.
- [ ] Update acquisition documents to require a penetration testing plan that clearly sets out the testing coverage (breadth), level of testing (depth), and any limits (constraints), aligned with sa-11.05_odp.01/02/03.
- [ ] Require end-to-end traceability from each scope item to the test case and the supporting evidence, covering networks, web applications, application programming interfaces (APIs), authentication, and privilege boundaries.
- [ ] Require penetration testing to include attempts to bypass login (authentication) and session controls, and to assess outcomes up to gaining higher-level access (privilege escalation) and any impact on access to data.
- [ ] Set contractual rules for approved testing time windows, safe operation for operational technology (OT), and a strict requirement not to use any exploits beyond the agreed scope.
- [ ] Require privacy controls for any captured personal data, including: minimising what is collected, protecting it, redacting sensitive information, setting retention limits, and obtaining confirmation that data is deleted or returned.
- [ ] Appoint an independent reviewer to check that the plan is complete, that the supporting evidence is high quality, and that it follows the agreed scope and constraints.


---

#### SA-11.6 — Attack Surface Reviews (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that whenever a system or service is changed, the people who build it carefully check every part that is exposed or accessible, to understand what new weaknesses those changes might create. Without this, updates and improvements can unintentionally create openings—for example, features that are not properly protected, unsafe functions, or gaps that were missed in the software, hardware, or underlying components—allowing criminals to exploit the system in ways the organisation did not expect.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must require the developer to carry out an attack surface review for every design or implementation change, analyse the changes to identify any new or increased attack risks, record those risks, and fix them by removing or deprecating unsafe functions where needed. The developer must also keep clear records showing that the review was completed, and what was found and corrected.

##### Change-triggered attack surface reviews with auditable remediation

- Category: Manual
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define ASR trigger criteria and decision logic for in-scope change types (interfaces, authz/authn flows, network listeners/ports, API endpoints, trust-boundary data flows, dependency/SDK upgrades, security posture configuration changes, firmware/agent updates) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create standard ASR template (minimum required sections, unsafe-function handling rules, risk/mitigation/verification mapping, acceptance criteria, and required sign-offs) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate ASR into SDLC/change workflow as a release gate (update change ticket/PR checklist, define required artefact linkage to release record, enforce pre-merge/pre-release completion for in-scope changes) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement auditable evidence capture and integrity (immutable repository location, ASR-to-ticket/PR-to-build/release linkage, build ID association, document hash generation, retention and access controls) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Establish security reviewer validation workflow (review checklist, completeness/quality criteria, approval/exception process for compensating controls, and unsafe-function decision governance) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define remediation acceptance criteria and verification approach (how mitigations are evidenced, required verification artefacts, retest/scan expectations, and closure rules for each risk item) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Pilot the end-to-end process on a representative set of recent changes and refine (measure cycle time, completeness, reviewer throughput, and evidence auditability; update template/workflow accordingly) | Service Delivery Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |

Total Estimated Effort: **200h**  
Total Estimated Cost: **£6,000**

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the criteria for when an automatic security review (ASR) is required for in-scope design or implementation changes that affect areas that are exposed or accessible.
- [ ] Create and publish a standard “ASR” template that requires: the scope, an analysis of possible attack methods, identification of risks, the planned mitigations, and actions to address any unsafe functions.
- [ ] Update the software development life cycle (SDLC) and change process so that, for in-scope changes, the security assessment report (ASR) is completed and attached to the change ticket before the change can be merged or released.
- [ ] Set up a way to store evidence that can be audited, and link it between automatic speech recognition (ASR) outputs, change tickets and pull requests (PRs), and build and release records.
- [ ] Set clear acceptance criteria for remediation that require documented fixes, and that specify the planned deprecation or removal of unsafe functions (or, where agreed, approved alternative compensating controls).
- [ ] Train developers and security reviewers on how to complete ASRs and on what to expect when unsafe functions are removed


---

#### SA-11.7 — Verify Scope of Testing and Evaluation (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the people who build or supply a system can prove that their security testing truly covers everything you need, completely and with strong confidence. Without this, important security weaknesses could be missed because some checks were not done, were not tested in every part of the system, or were only tested in a superficial way—leaving you with a false sense of safety.

The organisation must require the developer to formally link every required security measure, including any inherited or replacement measures, to specific test cases across all parts of the system and across how those parts connect to other systems. The developer must provide clear evidence that each test was carried out, the results of each test, and a documented review showing that the results confirm the measures are set up correctly and work as intended.

This must be supported by structured analysis, with records that can be traced back to the requirements, and it must be included in the testing plan, the test results, and the relevant procurement and contract documents.

##### Formal control-to-test coverage matrix with evidence gates

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Establish authoritative coverage inputs pack: required control list (incl. inherited/compensating), and component/interface inventory (architecture + data-flow + interface list) with version control | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define Coverage Matrix template and evidence-gate requirements (required fields, evidence reference formats, expected vs actual structure, reviewer sign-off workflow) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Developer formal mapping: produce control-to-test mapping matrix covering 100% of required controls across all components/interfaces, including test identifiers, test types, and explicit implementation/configuration linkages | Software Lead | Business Unit | 80h | — |
| Evidence capture and packaging: ensure each mapped test case has immutable execution evidence (e.g., CI job IDs/logs, report links, artefact hashes) and recorded results (expected vs actual) | QA/Test lead | Team | 56h | — |
| Results review records: conduct structured reviewer review per control cluster (or per control where needed), document discrepancies, root cause, remediation actions, and provide retest evidence / risk acceptance outcomes | Quality Assurance Lead | Team | 40h | — |
| Formal analysis/correlation rationale: provide structured justification correlating control implementation/configuration elements to test assertions; include model-based reasoning where feasible and document limitations | System Design Authority | Department | 32h | — |
| Acceptance gate validation: perform completeness checks (no unmapped controls, no missing evidence/results, inherited/compensating controls included, coverage spans declared interfaces, review records complete) and produce an acceptance decision pack | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 272h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish the official list of required security controls that developers must use when mapping, including any controls they inherit and any compensating controls.
- [ ] Provide an official list of components and interfaces (architecture, interface list, and a data-flow map) to define the scope of coverage for both breadth and depth.
- [ ] Require submission of a **control-to-test coverage matrix** that includes: **test case IDs**, the **components or interfaces covered**, the **expected results versus the actual results**, and **references to supporting evidence**.
- [ ] Set acceptance checks so delivery is blocked if any required control is not mapped, or if any mapped test does not have execution evidence and results.
- [ ] For each group of controls, require documented evidence that the results were reviewed, including how any differences were handled and proof of any retesting.
- [ ] Require a formal analysis and explanation showing how the way each control is implemented or configured links to the mapped test assertions.


---

#### SA-11.8 — Dynamic Code Analysis (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the software is tested while it is actually running, so clear security weaknesses are found early. If developers only review code on paper, they can miss problems that appear during real use, such as the software behaving incorrectly, handling data in an unsafe way, or allowing people to get more access than they should.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must require the person or team building the system, component, or service to use tools that monitor the running software to identify common security weaknesses, including memory errors and unauthorised privilege or access problems. The developer must then record what the testing found and provide those documented results to the organisation for review, so any weaknesses can be tracked and fixed as part of the wider development and assurance process.

##### Dynamic code analysis gate with documented evidence for releases

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define organisation-approved dynamic analysis policy (tool whitelist, in-scope runtime targets, required test duration, severity thresholds, release-block/exception rules, evidence requirements) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Select and procure dynamic analysis tooling (runtime instrumentation/sanitiser support, fuzz testing harness support, report generation) and confirm licensing/usage terms for CI/CD | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | £18,000 |
| Implement CI/CD release gate for dynamic analysis (pipeline stages, runtime instrumentation where feasible, failure conditions mapped to severity thresholds, build artefact retention) | DevOps Lead | Business Unit | 40h | — |
| Implement fuzz testing for defined input-handling surfaces (derive fuzz targets from API/message/upload surfaces, configure corpora/seeds, set time/coverage targets, integrate into pipeline gate) | Software Lead | Department | 32h | £6,000 |
| Create standard “Dynamic Code Analysis Report” template and evidence capture (raw tool outputs + structured report: components, tool versions, environment, findings summary, reproduction guidance, triage/remediation status) | Security Engineer | Department | 24h | — |
| Establish security review workflow and exception handling (AppSec review SLA, how to assess/approve exceptions, link approvals to release/version, audit trail requirements) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Operationalise third-party/vendor component evidence requirements (contractual evidence pack checklist, intake process, verification steps, and acceptance criteria for delivered builds) | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 172h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £24,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an organisation-approved dynamic analysis policy that sets out which tools are allowed, which systems are included, and the severity levels required to decide whether a release can go ahead.
- [ ] Update the continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipeline templates so that each release candidate build runs dynamic analysis and fuzz testing.
- [ ] Set up runtime monitoring for the supported components (for example, builds that include sanitiser checks) and make sure tests verify that users only have the required permissions and access.
- [ ] Create a standard dynamic code analysis report, and save the raw outputs from the analysis tools as unchangeable build records linked to the specific release or version.
- [ ] Add the findings to the defect or ticket workflow, and make sure the triage status is recorded in the evidence pack.
- [ ] Put in place release promotion controls to prevent deploying to production when security findings are above the agreed thresholds, unless there is documented security approval.

#### SA-11.9 — Interactive Application Security Testing (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that, before software is released, the people building it actively test the real, running application to find security weaknesses—not just rely on theory or a quick review. If this is not done, weaknesses may end up in live systems, where attackers could use them to steal data, disrupt services, or gain unauthorised access.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must require system developers (including suppliers) to use tools that observe the application while it is running, identify any security weaknesses they find, and then record the results in clear, auditable reports or findings. Your procurement and project documentation should set out these testing and evidence responsibilities. Your internal procedures should explain how staff should enforce them and what proof to keep. Project security records should show that this interactive testing took place and that the documented findings were tracked through to resolution, or to a formally accepted decision.

##### Contractual interactive testing evidence with release acceptance gates

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Draft contractual clause and schedule deliverable for “Interactive Application Security Testing (IAST) evidence pack” (SOW/SLAs/security addendum), including enforceable acceptance gate wording for release sign-off | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define minimum evidence pack content standard (scope, runtime/instrumentation enablement, execution windows, findings table schema, traceability to remediation tickets/risk acceptance decisions) and publish as an auditable template | Security Governance/Assurance team | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Update procurement and delivery governance workflow: integrate evidence submission requirements into release planning, change/release security review checklists, and sign-off criteria (fail/conditional/pass rules) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Establish organisation-controlled evidence repository guidance (naming conventions, access controls, retention expectations, review workflow) and provide an operational runbook for developers/vendors on how to submit the IAST evidence pack | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 18h | — |
| Create review and validation procedure for the Assurance team (completeness checks, traceability verification, sampling approach, escalation path for missing/insufficient evidence) | Security Governance/Assurance team | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Pilot the acceptance gate on 1–2 representative releases/components (including vendor-managed components where feasible) to confirm evidence sufficiency, adjust templates, and document lessons learned | Application Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £5,000 |
| Roll out the requirement across procurement and delivery teams (training, comms, and updated governance artefacts) and implement ongoing compliance monitoring cadence (e.g., per release reporting) | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 138h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £5,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Update the statement of work (SOW), service level agreements (SLAs), and security addendum templates to require interactive, instrumentation-based application security testing and documented test results.
- [ ] Define and publish a minimum “interactive application security testing (IAST)” evidence pack format, including: scope, evidence from the tools or instrumentation used, the time window during which testing was run, a findings table, and the disposition (outcome/decision).
- [ ] Add release acceptance gates that prevent approval (sign-off) when evidence from interactive testing or documented findings are missing.
- [ ] Ensure every documented finding can be traced to a corresponding remediation ticket or to a formally approved decision to accept the risk.
- [ ] Set up a process to submit evidence to a repository controlled by the organisation, and appoint reviewers to approve release security sign-off.
- [ ] For software-as-a-service (SaaS) and managed services, include in the contract a regular schedule for security reporting and the right to share evidence and carry out audits.

### SA-15 — Development Process, Standards, and Tools (Control)

This requirement is about making sure the people who build your software or services follow a clear, written way of working that protects sensitive information and personal data. Without this, developers may use the wrong methods or settings, make changes without the right approvals, or fail to include the right safeguards for Confidential and Secret information. That could result in unauthorised access, data leaks, or failing to meet legal and regulatory requirements such as the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) and the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR), as well as export and defence expectations.

The organisation must ensure the developer uses a documented development process that clearly covers both security and privacy needs. This process must name the standards and development tools to be used, including the exact tool options and configurations, and it must control changes to those tools and processes so that only authorised updates are made and the integrity of the tools and process is maintained.

The organisation must also review these choices at least quarterly, and after any major tool or process change or any material incident. The purpose is to confirm they still achieve the required outcomes for secure coding, risk analysis, finding and fixing weaknesses, limiting access, and maintaining integrity, as well as privacy measures such as data minimisation, access limits, and auditability.

##### Integrity-controlled SDLC baseline with tool config drift checks

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Establish Secure & Private SDLC baseline (single source of truth) with stage-gates and Confidential/Secret security & privacy requirements mapping | Secure SDLC/DevSecOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Define development standards and integrity expectations (secure coding, threat-modelling approach, vulnerability remediation expectations, least privilege, auditability) and publish as baseline artefacts | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create approved tool categories and exact configuration profiles (SAST/SCA/secrets scanning/build/artefact signing) including required options (ruleset versions, severity thresholds, logging destinations, retention, auth method, integrations) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement configuration control for baseline/tool profiles (version-controlled repository, change approval workflow, auditable change log linking approvals to affected projects) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Build CI/CD drift detection & enforcement (pipeline checks for approved tool profile hashes/versions, required steps present, secrets scanning enabled; block or flag non-compliant releases) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 64h | £18,000 |
| Integrate evidence capture for audits (generate immutable evidence bundles per build/release; retain logs/scan reports to agreed retention; provide quarterly review packs) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |
| Run quarterly reviews and event-driven reviews (after major tool/process changes or material incidents) using a maturity-model assessment; record outcomes, gaps, corrective actions, and update baseline/tool profiles via controlled change | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 280h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £24,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Publish a secure and private software development life cycle (SDLC) baseline that sets out the security and privacy requirements for Confidential and Secret data.
- [ ] Document approved development standards and link them to secure coding, threat modelling, vulnerability management, least privilege, and integrity controls.
- [ ] Define approved tool configuration profiles with the exact settings for each tool, including ruleset version, thresholds, logging and retention, and authentication requirements.
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) checks to confirm that tools are configured according to the required profiles and to spot any changes in tools or processes over time.
- [ ] Set up an authorised change process for updating the software development lifecycle (SDLC) baseline and tool settings, with approval records that can be audited and a complete version history.
- [ ] Schedule and carry out quarterly reviews of the software development lifecycle (SDLC) baseline and the tool settings. Record the results and any corrective actions needed.
- [ ] After any major change to a tool or process, or after any significant incident, carry out an additional review and record the results.

#### SA-15.1 — Quality Metrics (Enhancement)

This requirement is about agreeing in advance what “good quality” means for a new system, and then showing that it was achieved when the work is handed over. Without clear, checkable quality targets, a developer could produce something that appears complete but misses important requirements. This can lead to expensive rework, disruption to services, or weaknesses that only become clear after release.  

The organisation must therefore require the system developer to define measurable quality measures at the very start of development, including clear quality checkpoints at each key milestone. The developer must then provide evidence that the system meets these measures at handover, at each major development milestone, and again before release.  

Finally, the organisation must review progress against these quality measures at least every quarter through a programme review with security and privacy representatives, and record the results and any follow-up actions.

##### Quality Gate Pack with milestone evidence for delivery acceptance

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create organisation-controlled “Quality Gate Pack” template (metrics, stage-based gates, metric-to-evidence mapping, version/build binding fields) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define measurable quality metrics and explicit pass/fail criteria for delivery acceptance (including security/privacy thresholds and test/defect handling criteria) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Establish evidence submission schedule and acceptance workflow (milestone evidence requirements, delivery “upon delivery” anchor, exception handling and sign-off steps) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Configure/standardise CI/CD pipeline gate checks to produce auditable evidence artefacts (where feasible) and link outputs to build/version identifiers | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Implement Quality Gate Pack completion and validation checklist in release management (ensure no required metric lacks an evidence reference; enforce completeness before release) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Run quarterly programme review process using the Quality Gate Pack data (security & privacy attendance, recorded outcomes, follow-up actions, residual risk tracking) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Pilot the approach on one representative delivery and refine template/gates based on findings (lessons learned, evidence gaps, usability improvements) | Project Manager | Business Unit | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 176h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish a standard “Quality Gate Pack” template. It should include: a list of quality metrics, the quality checks required at each stage, and the requirements for linking each metric to the supporting evidence.
- [ ] Require developers to submit a dated quality metrics document and the definitions for quality checks at the start of each project (at the kickoff or planning approval stage).
- [ ] Require evidence to be submitted at every major development milestone, before each release, and at delivery. Each submission must be linked to a specific build or version identifier.
- [ ] Set minimum measurable quality requirements that match the organisation’s acceptable security and privacy risk levels (for example, common vulnerability scoring system (CVSS) thresholds, enough testing and defect coverage, and how compiler warnings should be handled).
- [ ] Create an acceptance checklist to confirm that all required evidence is complete and can be traced back to each required metric.
- [ ] Run a quarterly programme review with security and privacy representatives, using the structured Quality Gate Pack information, and record the results and any follow-up actions.

#### SA-15.2 — Security and Privacy Tracking Tools (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that the people building a system use the right tools to keep a clear, traceable record of both security and privacy work as it is being created. Without this, important fixes and privacy-related changes can be missed, delayed, or handled in different ways, which increases the risk that security weaknesses remain in the system or that personal information is used or protected incorrectly.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must require the system developer to select and use suitable tracking tools throughout the development process for:
- **Security work**, such as recording and managing security issues from discovery through to completion.
- **Privacy work**, such as recording and managing privacy tasks from identification through to completion.

The organisation should also keep evidence of which tools were selected and be able to show that the developer actually used them to assign responsibility, track progress, and record completion. This includes cases where systems are developed by third parties through procurement and contract requirements.

##### Approved security & privacy work-item tracking with pipeline evidence

- Category: Software
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define and document the approved security & privacy tracking tool list (including scope, ownership, and evidence expectations) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Configure standard security work-item template(s) in the approved tool(s) with required fields, labels/categories, and closure evidence requirements | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure standard privacy work-item template(s) in the approved tool(s) with required fields, labels/categories, and closure evidence requirements | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement CI/CD gate checks to enforce: required labels/categories, assignee present, at least one post-creation status update, and presence of required security/privacy work items by change classification | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 56h | £3,000 |
| Build evidence capture automation to export/query security/privacy work items by label and date range, and store in an append-only/immutable evidence repository | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Define and publish developer workflow guidance (how to create, update, and close work items; how evidence is generated; common failure modes) and run enablement sessions | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Extend requirements to third parties via onboarding/procurement artefacts (vendor onboarding checklist, contract addendum clauses, and audit/evidence obligations) | Procurement / Contract Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Perform pilot rollout across 1–2 representative pipelines, validate enforcement and evidence completeness, and remediate gaps before enterprise rollout | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £2,500 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 244h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £11,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Document and publish the organisation’s approved security and privacy tracking tools for use during software development.
- [ ] Set up security and privacy work-item templates that include the required fields, clear labels, and proof of closure.
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) “policy gates” so that security and privacy work items are in place before code can be merged or released. This includes having an assigned owner, the correct labels, and the work item moving through the required status steps.
- [ ] Automatically export or retrieve evidence from the tracking tools, using the security and privacy labels to filter what is included, and store the results with write-once, unchangeable retention.
- [ ] Update vendor onboarding and/or procurement contract requirements to require the use of the approved tracking tools and to specify what evidence must be provided.


---

#### SA-15.3 — Criticality Analysis (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the people building a system carefully consider what could happen if the system were harmed, before it is built and every time it is changed. Without this, serious problems could be missed—such as sensitive information being exposed, data being altered, services becoming unavailable, or safety being put at risk—especially when the system depends on bought-in products, third-party services, or supplier components.

To meet this expectation, the system developer must carry out a full criticality analysis of the entire system, including every component and connection. This must cover confidentiality (keeping information private), integrity (keeping data accurate and unaltered), availability (keeping services working), and safety (preventing harm). It must also explicitly consider supply-chain risks. This work must be done at each key stage: when requirements are first defined, throughout design, before implementation, after any major change, and for every release.

The analysis must use the organisation’s documented impact ratings. It must be supported by realistic examples of how harm could occur, a clear description of how information flows through the system, and links showing how the results connect to the relevant security measures and the organisation’s mission impact.

##### Developer criticality analysis gates with traceable CIA+Safety

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the criticality model schema (versioned template) covering component/interface inventory, CIA impact, safety impact, data-flow mapping references, threat-informed scenarios, supply-chain fields, and traceability to security controls and mission impact | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement repository-backed criticality model artefact structure (including validation hooks/CI checks for completeness and traceability at each required decision point) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 56h | £6,000 |

**Total Estimated Cost:** £11,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a version-controlled template for a criticality model that covers: a list of components and interfaces, references to how data moves through the system, impact ratings for confidentiality, integrity, availability and safety, threat-informed scenarios, supply-chain considerations, and traceability from security controls to mission impact.
- [ ] Set up software development lifecycle (SDLC) checkpoints so that the criticality model is required at the concept and requirements stage, during design, before implementation, after major changes, and for every release.
- [ ] Set up automated checks to confirm that every component and interface has assigned “confidentiality, integrity, availability (CIA)” and safety ratings, based on documented impact levels and a clear link from each scenario to the data flow and then to the control.
- [ ] Set up and enforce a supplier evidence intake process for commercial off-the-shelf (COTS) and third-party services. This should capture supply-chain considerations and record any assumptions and limitations.
- [ ] Carry out a security architecture review at each project gate to confirm that each scenario is high quality and correct, and to verify that the chosen impact areas for confidentiality, integrity, availability (CIA) and safety are selected correctly and can be traced back to their sources.
- [ ] Store and label the criticality model file for each release in an unchangeable, audit-ready repository that keeps a complete record of changes.


---

#### SA-15.5 — Attack Surface Reduction (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making a system “smaller and harder to attack” before it goes live. It does this by removing anything that is not needed and by flagging anything that is already known to be unsafe. If unused features, open communication points, leftover user accounts, or unnecessary ways for other software to connect are left in place, criminals have more opportunities to find weaknesses and break in, steal data, or disrupt services.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set clear rules for what must be removed or disabled. It must then make sure the system developer follows these rules before release by removing or turning off unused services, network ports, accounts, and application connections, and by disabling unsafe functions ahead of release.

The organisation also needs to build these expectations into procurement and development processes. This means requiring them in bids, contracts, and service agreements, documenting how the reduction will be carried out in design and security plans, and keeping evidence that the changes were completed and checked before the release date.

##### CI/CD attack surface baseline gate for release candidates

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the organisation-controlled “restricted/allowed exposure model” (services/ports/protocols, accounts/service principals, API routes/versions, unsafe/deprecated functions) including threshold semantics and exception handling requirements | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design the CI/CD gate architecture and evidence contract (what the pipeline must export; evidence bundle schema; pass/fail logic; mapping to SA-15(5) enhancement) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement build-time attack surface inventory collectors for target runtime images and application artefacts (listening services/ports/protocols, API route manifest/OpenAPI-derived routes, enabled feature flags) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Implement identity/account/service principal inventory extraction for the component (container runtime users, service identities, application service accounts) and normalise into the evidence bundle | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | £4,000 |
| Implement unsafe/deprecated function detection and enforcement (allow/deny lists; static analysis findings mapped to unsafe functions; ensure “deprecated” state is operationally enforced) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 28h | £8,000 |
| Develop policy-as-code checks and release candidate blocking rules (threshold comparisons, disallowed/unused exposure detection, exception evidence validation, deterministic reporting) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate the gate into CI/CD and release promotion workflow (pipeline stages, failure messaging, developer remediation guidance, audit-ready evidence bundle publication) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Pilot rollout on 1–2 representative services, tune thresholds/false positives, and produce a sign-off pack demonstrating gate effectiveness and audit readiness | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 188h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £18,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set and publish the organisation-approved baseline limits for the attack surface of services, including which ports and protocols are allowed, which accounts and service principals can be used, which application programming interfaces (APIs) are allowed, and which unsafe functions are not permitted (sa-15.05_odp).
- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) to collect an inventory of what is included in each release. Export, for the release package, the services and ports, the application programming interface (API) route list, the enabled feature settings, and the relevant account or service identity evidence.
- [ ] Create policy-as-code rules that compare the exported inventory against the baseline and stop the promotion if any prohibited or unused exposure, or any unsafe functions, are detected.
- [ ] Make sure unsafe functions are no longer used by default in production releases by disabling or protecting them, and ensure the release files include the documentation explaining which functions are deprecated.
- [ ] For each release candidate, create and store a complete set of audit-ready evidence (a snapshot of what is in place, the results of policy checks, and a list of any items that were removed or disabled) to support the system security plan and release approval.
- [ ] Link the gate to the release process so that only artefacts approved by the pipeline can be promoted to production environments.


---

#### SA-15.6 — Continuous Improvement (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the people who build or maintain your system do not treat development as a one-time task. Instead, they must run an ongoing, documented improvement routine that keeps improving how they build and maintain the system over time. Without this, quality can gradually decline, the same mistakes can happen again, and the system may not keep pace with new security and privacy risks as the outside world changes.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must require the developer to cover all development work used to build, change, or maintain the system. The developer must also regularly check whether their approach is meeting the agreed quality goals in an efficient and effective way. In addition, they must review how well their process supports the security and privacy capabilities needed for today’s risk environment, using the results from security and privacy assessments and quality reviews as input.

The developer must set measurable improvement goals, record the actions they will take, assign responsibility, set milestone dates, and keep these updates in the relevant procurement and contract records (including service agreements where used). This ensures progress can be tracked and overseen by the appropriate internal roles.

##### Contractual continuous improvement evidence packs with measurable cadence

- Category: Manual
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Update enterprise acquisition policy/procedures to require continuous improvement evidence packs for relevant development procurements (including managed service providers) | Procurement/Commercial lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Revise contract templates/contract schedules (incl. SLAs) to include: named evidence pack deliverable, minimum content, cadence, two-period continuity requirement, acceptance/rejection criteria, and audit/traceability expectations | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Define the standard “Continuous Improvement Evidence Pack” specification (minimum fields, evidence mapping approach, metric definitions, traceability rules, and before/after measurable change requirement) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Establish quality/security/privacy objectives mapping guidance (how developers map effectiveness/efficiency metrics to agreed objectives; how security/privacy review inputs are referenced and evidenced) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 232h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Update the acquisition policy and procedures to require continuous improvement deliverables under SA-15(6) for relevant developer procurements.
- [ ] Update the tender and contract templates to add a “Continuous Improvement Evidence Pack” schedule item, including the minimum required contents.
- [ ] Define the agreed quality targets and the effectiveness and efficiency measures the developer must report each period.
- [ ] Set a regular reporting schedule and require proof of progress in at least two consecutive reporting periods, with time-bound improvement milestones.
- [ ] Assign internal responsibility for contract ownership and technical review for receiving, checking, and approving evidence packs.
- [ ] Put in place contract acceptance checks that confirm there is a clear link (traceability) from the evidence gathered during security, privacy, and quality assessments to the documented improvement actions.

#### SA-15.7 — Automated Vulnerability Analysis (Enhancement)

This requirement is about regularly checking your system for known security weaknesses, and doing the same immediately after any code or configuration change. The checks should be automated and should include reviewing the code itself, testing the running service, checking third-party components, and scanning any packaged software images. This matters because weaknesses that are not discovered or assessed can be used by criminals to break in, steal data, or disrupt services—especially after new changes are introduced.

To meet this expectation, the system developer must run these automated checks every week and after each code change or configuration update. If any issues are found, the developer must assess how easily they could be exploited and identify practical ways to reduce the risk, such as fixes or other risk-reducing measures.

The developer must then share the scan results and conclusions—including how likely the issues are to be exploited and the proposed mitigations—with the system owner and the vulnerability management lead every week and after each change.

##### CI/CD automated vulnerability analysis with exploitation triage

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define CI/CD security workflow requirements and evidence schema (build/version identifiers, trigger conditions, finding enrichment fields for exploitation potential + mitigations, delivery destinations) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Select/confirm tooling integrations for SAST, SCA (incl. SBOM generation), container/image scanning, and DAST (including feasibility for ephemeral test deployment) and document configuration constraints | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |
| Implement CI/CD pipeline triggers (weekly scheduled run + post-merge and configuration-update events) and standardise execution across repositories/build types | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Integrate SAST + SCA into the pipeline, ensuring results are bound to commit hash/build ID and SBOM artefacts are generated/attached where supported | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Integrate container/image vulnerability scanning for produced images (digest-based traceability), normalise findings, and ensure outputs are captured in the evidence package | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £3,000 |
| Implement DAST stage with safe ephemeral deployment (or, where not feasible, implement documented skip logic with compensating evidence requirements) and bind results to the same build/version | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £2,000 |
| Build the “vulnerability analysis package” generator and enrichment workflow (consolidation of tool outputs, structured exploitation-potential judgement, mitigation recommendation record, and audit-ready packaging) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 256h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £11,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set up continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipeline triggers to run on a weekly schedule and automatically after any code or configuration changes.
- [ ] Make static application security testing (SAST), software composition analysis (SCA), and container and image vulnerability scanning mandatory steps in the workflow.
- [ ] Set up a temporary test or staging environment and run dynamic application security testing (DAST) using the same build or version.
- [ ] Implement a consolidation step that links all findings to the build or version identifier and the reference to the change that triggered them.
- [ ] Create a workflow that, for each finding, assesses its potential for exploitation and recommends mitigations, and then produces structured results for that finding.
- [ ] Automate the creation of one complete evidence pack and securely send it to the system owner and the vulnerability management lead.

#### SA-15.8 — Reuse of Threat and Vulnerability Information (Enhancement)

This requirement is about learning from similar systems before you build or change your own, so you do not repeat the same mistakes. It matters because attackers often take advantage of the same types of weaknesses across comparable products. If you only assess risks from the beginning, you may miss well-known problem patterns, which can lead to expensive fixes, service disruption, or the loss of sensitive information.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must ensure the system developer uses “threat thinking” (identifying likely ways harm could happen) and “vulnerability reviews” (checking known weaknesses) based on similar systems, components, or services. The developer must then use the findings to make real development decisions, such as design choices, requirements, and implementation guidance.

The organisation should make this reuse a required part of the development process. It should be written into relevant development procedures and security plans, and included in procurement documents and contracts so it is enforceable when buying or commissioning services.

##### Threat/vuln reuse library with traceable design decision mapping

- Category: Software
- Priority: High

|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define similarity selection criteria and evidence schema (threat/vuln reference metadata, “why similar” rationale, required mapping fields, exception/waiver process) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish governance for the similarity reference library (ownership, contribution workflow, review/approval, versioning, retention, and audit controls) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Build the similarity reference library (data model + repository structure for threat models and vulnerability analyses; ingestion templates for internal artefacts and external advisories such as CVE/NVD; access controls) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £6,000 |
| Implement traceable mapping workflow and CI/CD/release gate (required fields, validation rules, evidence packaging, gate fail/override with approved exception) integrated with issue tracker and ADR/ticket links | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 64h | £12,000 |
| Create developer-facing guidance and templates (how to select similar references, how to populate mapping to design/implementation decisions, examples, and training materials) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

| Operationalise periodic review of library and mappings (scheduled revalidation cadence, dependency/advisory change triggers, and reporting for governance/audit) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 264h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £18,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish the rules for selecting similar systems to reuse in threat modelling and vulnerability analysis, including architecture, trust boundaries, the authentication model, data classification, and integration points.
- [ ] Create a curated library of known threats and vulnerabilities, with supporting details (metadata) and a clear explanation of why each item is similar to the others in the library.
- [ ] Set up a development workflow checkpoint that requires developers to choose reference IDs and provide traceable links between those IDs and the design and implementation decisions they made.
- [ ] Add evidence capture to the tools you already use (issue tracker, architecture decision records, and design review checklists) so that the required mappings are created and kept automatically.
- [ ] Add automated checks to confirm the submission is complete (including required fields, a minimum number of threat and vulnerability references, and links to the decisions) so it cannot be released without supporting evidence.
- [ ] Set up a regular review of the library to update references when dependencies change or when new security advisories are issued.

#### SA-15.10 — Incident Response Plan (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that, if something goes wrong, the people who build the system already have a clear, tested plan for how to respond. Without an incident response plan that is actually used and checked through testing, serious problems such as a security breach, service disruption, or misuse could be dealt with in different ways. This could lead to delays, more damage, and confusion about who should do what.  

To meet this expectation, the system developer must provide the organisation with an incident response plan for the specific system, component, or service, ensure it is followed in day-to-day operations, and test it to confirm it works in real situations. The developer must also share the plan in a usable format so the organisation can incorporate it into its own arrangements for handling incidents.

- [ ] Add incident response plan (IR plan) pack deliverables and acceptance criteria to the statement of work (SOW) and master services agreement (MSA) for each developer or vendor system component.
- [ ] Define the required proof of implementation, including: on-call and incident responsibilities, how the process connects to ticketing and workflow tools, and extracts from the runbook that show day-to-day execution.
- [ ] Define what testing proof is required, including tabletop and technical validation scenarios, the results, and the remediation actions (with closure dates).
- [ ] Create a vendor onboarding checklist to gather, review, and approve the incident response plan pack before the system goes live and after any major changes.
- [ ] Document an internal process for adding the approved developer incident response plan pack into the organisation’s incident response arrangements.

#### SA-15.11 — Archive System or Component (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that when a supplier delivers a system or component, they also provide a complete “archive pack” showing what they built and the evidence that it was checked and approved for both security and privacy. This is important because if you only receive the finished product, you may not be able to confirm what was included, correct issues later, or demonstrate to regulators and customers that the final checks were completed properly. This can result in costly delays, weaker oversight, and avoidable risk.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must require in its purchasing and contract arrangements that the developer prepares and archives the delivered system or component before delivery. The archive pack must be provided together with the evidence used to support the final security and privacy review, including key development materials such as hardware details, the human-readable build code, the compiled release files, and the relevant build and configuration documentation. It must be packaged in a way that gives a clear starting point for future updates.

- [ ] Update the contract and statement of work (SOW) templates to require the developer to archive the exact component that is being released or delivered before delivery, and to include the final security and privacy review evidence.
- [ ] Set out the minimum information that must be kept in the archive for your application (source code, compiled code, and the relevant build and configuration documents; include hardware specifications where they apply).
- [ ] Set up an automated check that confirms the archive is complete, that the version and build match the final review records, and that the evidence references are consistent with those records.
- [ ] During acceptance testing, run a retrieval test (read-only download plus checksum verification) and record the results in the acceptance evidence pack.
- [ ] Store the archive package and acceptance logs in the organisation’s secure, controlled repository, with access restricted to authorised roles.
